Recognising that these dissidents could cause problems for their Russian enemies, the German government agreed to permit 32 Russian citizens to travel by train through their territory, among them Lenin and his wife.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964109–110Rice1990139Pipes1990386,_389–391Service2000255–256White2001127–128_131-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964109%E2%80%93110Rice1990139Pipes1990386,_389%E2%80%93391Service2000255%E2%80%93256White2001127%E2%80%93128-131">[128]</a></sup> For political reasons, Lenin and the Germans agreed to a [cover story](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Disinformation "Disinformation") that Lenin had travelled by [sealed train](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sealed_train "Sealed train") carriage through German territory, but in fact the train was not truly sealed, and the passengers were allowed to disembark to, for example, spend the night in Frankfurt.<sup id="cite_ref-132"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-132">[129]</a></sup> The group travelled by train from Zürich to [Sassnitz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sassnitz "Sassnitz"), proceeding by ferry to [Trelleborg](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trelleborg "Trelleborg"), Sweden, and from there to the [Haparanda](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Haparanda "Haparanda")–[Tornio](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tornio "Tornio") border crossing and then to [Helsinki](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Helsinki "Helsinki") before taking the final train to Petrograd in disguise.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964110–113Rice1990140–144Pipes1990391–392Service2000257–260_133-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964110%E2%80%93113Rice1990140%E2%80%93144Pipes1990391%E2%80%93392Service2000257%E2%80%93260-133">[130]</a></sup>

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/The_locomotive_M-293%2C_which_in_August_1917_Lenin_went_to_Finland.JPG/170px-The_locomotive_M-293%2C_which_in_August_1917_Lenin_went_to_Finland.JPG)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:The_locomotive_M-293,_which_in_August_1917_Lenin_went_to_Finland.JPG)

The engine that pulled the train on which Lenin arrived at Petrograd's [Finland Station](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Finland_Station "Finland Station") in April 1917 was not preserved. So Engine #293, by which Lenin escaped to Finland and then returned to Russia later in the year, serves as the permanent exhibit, installed at a platform on the station.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMerridale2017ix_134-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMerridale2017ix-134">[131]</a></sup>

Arriving at Petrograd's [Finland Station](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Finland_Station "Finland Station") in April, Lenin gave a speech to Bolshevik supporters condemning the Provisional Government and again calling for a continent-wide European proletarian revolution.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964113,_124Rice1990144Pipes1990392Service2000261White2001131–132_135-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964113,_124Rice1990144Pipes1990392Service2000261White2001131%E2%80%93132-135">[132]</a></sup> Over the following days, he spoke at Bolshevik meetings, lambasting those who wanted reconciliation with the Mensheviks and revealing his "[April Theses](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/April_Theses "April Theses")", an outline of his plans for the Bolsheviks, which he had written on the journey from Switzerland.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPipes1990393–394Service2000266White2001132–135Read2005143,_146–147_136-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPipes1990393%E2%80%93394Service2000266White2001132%E2%80%93135Read2005143,_146%E2%80%93147-136">[133]</a></sup> He publicly condemned both the Mensheviks and the Social Revolutionaries, who dominated the influential [Petrograd Soviet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Petrograd_Soviet "Petrograd Soviet"), for supporting the Provisional Government, denouncing them as traitors to socialism. Considering the government to be just as imperialist as the Tsarist regime, he advocated immediate peace with Germany and Austria-Hungary, rule by [soviets](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_(council) "Soviet (council)"), the nationalisation of industry and banks, and the state expropriation of land, all with the intention of establishing a proletariat government and pushing toward a socialist society. By contrast, the Mensheviks believed that Russia was insufficiently developed to transition to socialism and accused Lenin of trying to plunge the new Republic into civil war.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEService2000266–268,_279White2001134–136Read2005147,_148_137-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEService2000266%E2%80%93268,_279White2001134%E2%80%93136Read2005147,_148-137">[134]</a></sup> Over the coming months Lenin campaigned for his policies, attending the meetings of the Bolshevik Central Committee, prolifically writing for the Bolshevik newspaper _[Pravda](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pravda "Pravda")_, and giving public speeches in Petrograd aimed at converting workers, soldiers, sailors, and peasants to his cause.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEService2000267,_271–272Read2005152,_154_138-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEService2000267,_271%E2%80%93272Read2005152,_154-138">[135]</a></sup>

Sensing growing frustration among Bolshevik supporters, Lenin suggested an armed political demonstration in Petrograd to test the government's response.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEService2000282Read2005157_139-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEService2000282Read2005157-139">[136]</a></sup> Amid deteriorating health, he left the city to recuperate in the Finnish village of Neivola.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPipes1990421Rice1990147Service2000276,_283White2001140Read2005157_140-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPipes1990421Rice1990147Service2000276,_283White2001140Read2005157-140">[137]</a></sup> The Bolsheviks' armed demonstration, the [July Days](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/July_Days "July Days"), took place while Lenin was away, but upon learning that demonstrators had violently clashed with government forces, he returned to Petrograd and called for calm.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPipes1990422–425Rice1990147–148Service2000283–284Read2005158–61White2001140–141Read2005157–159_141-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPipes1990422%E2%80%93425Rice1990147%E2%80%93148Service2000283%E2%80%93284Read2005158%E2%80%9361White2001140%E2%80%93141Read2005157%E2%80%93159-141">[138]</a></sup> Responding to the violence, the government ordered the arrest of Lenin and other prominent Bolsheviks, raiding their offices, and publicly alleging that he was a German _[agent provocateur](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Agent_provocateur "Agent provocateur")_.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPipes1990431–434Rice1990148Service2000284–285White2001141Read2005161_142-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPipes1990431%E2%80%93434Rice1990148Service2000284%E2%80%93285White2001141Read2005161-142">[139]</a></sup> Evading arrest, Lenin hid in a series of Petrograd [safe houses](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Safe_house "Safe house").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964125Rice1990148–149Service2000285_143-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964125Rice1990148%E2%80%93149Service2000285-143">[140]</a></sup> Fearing that he would be killed, Lenin and fellow senior Bolshevik [Grigory Zinoviev](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grigory_Zinoviev "Grigory Zinoviev") escaped Petrograd in disguise, relocating to [Razliv](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Razliv "Razliv").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPipes1990436,_467Service2000287White2001141Read2005165_144-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPipes1990436,_467Service2000287White2001141Read2005165-144">[141]</a></sup> There, Lenin began work on the book that became _[The State and Revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_State_and_Revolution "The State and Revolution")_, an exposition on how he believed the socialist state would develop after the proletariat revolution, and how from then on the state would gradually wither away, leaving a [pure communist society](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pure_communism "Pure communism").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPipes1990468–469Rice1990149Service2000289White2001142–143Read2005166–172_145-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPipes1990468%E2%80%93469Rice1990149Service2000289White2001142%E2%80%93143Read2005166%E2%80%93172-145">[142]</a></sup> He began arguing for a Bolshevik-led armed insurrection to topple the government, but at a clandestine meeting of the party's central committee this idea was rejected.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEService2000288_146-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEService2000288-146">[143]</a></sup> Lenin then headed by train and by foot to Finland, arriving at Helsinki on 10 August, where he hid away in safe houses belonging to Bolshevik sympathisers.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPipes1990468Rice1990150Service2000289–292Read2005165_147-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPipes1990468Rice1990150Service2000289%E2%80%93292Read2005165-147">[144]</a></sup>

### October Revolution: 1917

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Brodskiy%27s_Lenin.jpg/220px-Brodskiy%27s_Lenin.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Brodskiy%27s_Lenin.jpg)

Painting of Lenin in front of the [Smolny Institute](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Smolny_Institute "Smolny Institute") by [Isaak Brodsky](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Isaak_Brodsky "Isaak Brodsky")

In August 1917, while Lenin was in Finland, [General Lavr Kornilov](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lavr_Kornilov "Lavr Kornilov"), the Commander-in-Chief of the Russian Army, sent troops to Petrograd in what appeared to be a [military coup attempt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kornilov_Affair "Kornilov Affair") against the Provisional Government. Premier [Alexander Kerensky](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_Kerensky "Alexander Kerensky") turned to the Petrograd Soviet, including its Bolshevik members, for help, allowing the revolutionaries to organise workers as [Red Guards](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_Guards_(Russia) "Red Guards (Russia)") to defend the city. The coup petered out before it reached Petrograd, but the events had allowed the Bolsheviks to return to the open political arena.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPipes1990439–465Rice1990150–151Service2000299White2001143–144Read2005173_148-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPipes1990439%E2%80%93465Rice1990150%E2%80%93151Service2000299White2001143%E2%80%93144Read2005173-148">[145]</a></sup> Fearing a counter-revolution from right-wing forces hostile to socialism, the Mensheviks and Socialist-Revolutionaries who dominated the Petrograd Soviet had been instrumental in pressuring the government to normalise relations with the Bolsheviks.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPipes1990465_149-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPipes1990465-149">[146]</a></sup> Both the Mensheviks and Socialist-Revolutionaries had lost much popular support because of their affiliation with the Provisional Government and its unpopular continuation of the war. The Bolsheviks capitalised on this, and soon the pro-Bolshevik Marxist Trotsky was elected leader of the Petrograd Soviet.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPipes1990465–467White2001144Lee200317Read2005174_150-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPipes1990465%E2%80%93467White2001144Lee200317Read2005174-150">[147]</a></sup> In September, the Bolsheviks gained a majority in the workers' sections of both the Moscow and Petrograd Soviets.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPipes1990471Rice1990151–152Read2005180_151-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPipes1990471Rice1990151%E2%80%93152Read2005180-151">[148]</a></sup>

Recognising that the situation was safer for him, Lenin returned to Petrograd.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPipes1990473,_482Rice1990152Service2000302–303Read2005179_152-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPipes1990473,_482Rice1990152Service2000302%E2%80%93303Read2005179-152">[149]</a></sup> There he attended a meeting of the Bolshevik Central Committee on 10 October, where he again argued that the party should lead an armed insurrection to topple the Provisional Government. This time the argument won with ten votes against two.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPipes1990482–484Rice1990153–154Service2000303–304White2001146–147_153-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPipes1990482%E2%80%93484Rice1990153%E2%80%93154Service2000303%E2%80%93304White2001146%E2%80%93147-153">[150]</a></sup> Critics of the plan, Zinoviev and Kamenev, argued that Russian workers would not support a violent coup against the regime and that there was no clear evidence for Lenin's assertion that all of Europe was on the verge of proletarian revolution.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPipes1990471–472Service2000304White2001147_154-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPipes1990471%E2%80%93472Service2000304White2001147-154">[151]</a></sup> The party began plans to organise the offensive, holding a final meeting at the [Smolny Institute](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Smolny_Institute "Smolny Institute") on 24 October.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEService2000306–307_155-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEService2000306%E2%80%93307-155">[152]</a></sup> This was the base of the [Military Revolutionary Committee](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Military_Revolutionary_Committee "Military Revolutionary Committee") (MRC), an armed militia largely loyal to the Bolsheviks that had been established by the Petrograd Soviet during Kornilov's alleged coup.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERigby197914–15Leggett19811–3Pipes1990466Rice1990155_156-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTERigby197914%E2%80%9315Leggett19811%E2%80%933Pipes1990466Rice1990155-156">[153]</a></sup>

In October, the MRC was ordered to take control of Petrograd's key transport, communication, printing and utilities hubs, and did so without bloodshed.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPipes1990485–486,_491Rice1990157,_159Service2000308_157-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPipes1990485%E2%80%93486,_491Rice1990157,_159Service2000308-157">[154]</a></sup> Bolsheviks besieged the government in the [Winter Palace](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Winter_Palace "Winter Palace") and overcame it and arrested its ministers after the cruiser _[Aurora](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_cruiser_Aurora "Russian cruiser Aurora")_, controlled by Bolshevik seamen, fired a blank shot to signal the start of the revolution.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPipes1990492–493,_496Service2000311Read2005182_158-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPipes1990492%E2%80%93493,_496Service2000311Read2005182-158">[155]</a></sup> During the insurrection, Lenin gave a speech to the Petrograd Soviet announcing that the Provisional Government had been overthrown.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPipes1990491Service2000309_159-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPipes1990491Service2000309-159">[156]</a></sup> The Bolsheviks declared the formation of a new government, the [Council of People's Commissars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Council_of_People%27s_Commissars "Council of People's Commissars"), or Sovnarkom. Lenin initially turned down the leading position of [Chairman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Premier_of_the_Soviet_Union "Premier of the Soviet Union"), suggesting Trotsky for the job, but other Bolsheviks insisted and ultimately Lenin relented.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPipes1990499Service2000314–315_160-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPipes1990499Service2000314%E2%80%93315-160">[157]</a></sup> Lenin and other Bolsheviks then attended the [Second Congress of Soviets](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/All-Russian_Congress_of_Soviets#Second_Congress "All-Russian Congress of Soviets") on 26 and 27 October and announced the creation of the new government. Menshevik attendees condemned the illegitimate seizure of power and the risk of civil war.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPipes1990496–497Rice1990159–161Service2000314–315Read2005183_161-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPipes1990496%E2%80%93497Rice1990159%E2%80%93161Service2000314%E2%80%93315Read2005183-161">[158]</a></sup> In these early days of the new regime, Lenin avoided talking in Marxist and socialist terms so as not to alienate Russia's population, and instead spoke about having a country controlled by the workers.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPipes1990504Service2000315_162-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPipes1990504Service2000315-162">[159]</a></sup><sup>[<i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Accuracy_dispute#Disputed_statement" title="Wikipedia:Accuracy dispute"><span title="The material near this tag is possibly inaccurate or nonfactual. (January 2022)">dubious</span></a> <span>– <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Talk:Vladimir_Lenin#Dubious" title="Talk:Vladimir Lenin">discuss</a></span></i>]</sup> Lenin and many other Bolsheviks expected proletariat revolution to sweep across Europe in days or months.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEService2000316_163-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEService2000316-163">[160]</a></sup>

## Lenin's government

### Organising the Soviet government: 1917–1918

The Provisional Government had planned for a Constituent Assembly to be elected in November 1917; against Lenin's objections, Sovnarkom agreed for the vote to take place as scheduled.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShub1966314Service2000317_164-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShub1966314Service2000317-164">[161]</a></sup> In the [constitutional election](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1917_Russian_Constituent_Assembly_election "1917 Russian Constituent Assembly election"), the Bolsheviks gained approximately a quarter of the vote, being defeated by the agrarian-focused Socialist-Revolutionaries.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShub1966315Pipes1990540–541Rice1990164Volkogonov1994173Service2000331Read2005192_165-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShub1966315Pipes1990540%E2%80%93541Rice1990164Volkogonov1994173Service2000331Read2005192-165">[162]</a></sup> Lenin argued that the election was not a fair reflection of the people's will, that the electorate had not had time to learn the Bolsheviks' political programme, and that the candidacy lists had been drawn up before the Left Socialist-Revolutionaries split from the Socialist-Revolutionaries.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1994176Service2000331–332White2001156Read2005192_166-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1994176Service2000331%E2%80%93332White2001156Read2005192-166">[163]</a></sup> Nevertheless, the newly elected [Russian Constituent Assembly](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Constituent_Assembly "Russian Constituent Assembly") convened in Petrograd in January 1918.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERice1990164_167-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTERice1990164-167">[164]</a></sup> Sovnarkom argued that it was counter-revolutionary because it sought to remove power from the soviets, but the Socialist-Revolutionaries and Mensheviks denied this.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPipes1990546–547_168-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPipes1990546%E2%80%93547-168">[165]</a></sup> The Bolsheviks presented the Assembly with a motion that would strip it of most of its legal powers; when the Assembly rejected the motion, Sovnarkom declared this as evidence of its counter-revolutionary nature and forcibly disbanded it.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPipes1990552–553Rice1990165Volkogonov1994176–177Service2000332,_336–337Read2005192_169-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPipes1990552%E2%80%93553Rice1990165Volkogonov1994176%E2%80%93177Service2000332,_336%E2%80%93337Read2005192-169">[166]</a></sup>

Lenin rejected repeated calls, including from some Bolsheviks, to establish a coalition government with other socialist parties.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964158Shub1966301–302Rigby197926Leggett19815Pipes1990508,_519Service2000318–319Read2005189–190_170-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964158Shub1966301%E2%80%93302Rigby197926Leggett19815Pipes1990508,_519Service2000318%E2%80%93319Read2005189%E2%80%93190-170">[167]</a></sup> Although refusing a coalition with the Mensheviks or Socialist-Revolutionaries, Sovnarkom partially relented; they allowed the Left Socialist-Revolutionaries five posts in the cabinet in December 1917. This coalition only lasted four months until March 1918, when the Left Socialist-Revolutionaries pulled out of the government over a disagreement about the Bolsheviks' approach to ending the First World War.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERigby1979166–167Leggett198120–21Pipes1990533–534,_537Volkogonov1994171Service2000322–323White2001159Read2005191_171-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTERigby1979166%E2%80%93167Leggett198120%E2%80%9321Pipes1990533%E2%80%93534,_537Volkogonov1994171Service2000322%E2%80%93323White2001159Read2005191-171">[168]</a></sup> At their [7th Congress](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/7th_Congress_of_the_Russian_Communist_Party_(Bolsheviks) "7th Congress of the Russian Communist Party (Bolsheviks)") in March 1918, the Bolsheviks changed their official name from the Russian Social Democratic Labour Party to the Russian Communist Party, as Lenin wanted to both distance his group from the increasingly reformist German Social Democratic Party and to emphasise its ultimate goal, that of a communist society.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964219,_256,_379Shub1966374Service2000355White2001159Read2005219_172-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964219,_256,_379Shub1966374Service2000355White2001159Read2005219-172">[169]</a></sup>

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Kremlin_birds_eye_view-1.jpg/220px-Kremlin_birds_eye_view-1.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Kremlin_birds_eye_view-1.jpg)

The Moscow Kremlin, which Lenin moved into in 1918 (_pictured in 1987_)

Although ultimate power officially rested with the country's government in the form of Sovnarkom and the [Executive Committee](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/All-Russian_Central_Executive_Committee "All-Russian Central Executive Committee") (VTSIK) elected by the [All-Russian Congress of Soviets](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/All-Russian_Congress_of_Soviets "All-Russian Congress of Soviets") (ARCS), the Communist Party was _de facto_ in control in Russia, as acknowledged by its members at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERigby1979160–164Volkogonov1994374–375Service2000377_173-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTERigby1979160%E2%80%93164Volkogonov1994374%E2%80%93375Service2000377-173">[170]</a></sup> By 1918, Sovnarkom began acting unilaterally, claiming a need for expediency, with the ARCS and VTSIK becoming increasingly marginalised,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESandle199974Rigby1979168–169_174-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTESandle199974Rigby1979168%E2%80%93169-174">[171]</a></sup> so the soviets no longer had a role in governing Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964432_175-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964432-175">[172]</a></sup> During 1918 and 1919, the government expelled Mensheviks and Socialist-Revolutionaries from the soviets.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeggett1981316Lee200398–99_176-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeggett1981316Lee200398%E2%80%9399-176">[173]</a></sup> Russia had become a [one-party state](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/One-party_state "One-party state").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERigby1979160–161Leggett198121Lee200399_177-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTERigby1979160%E2%80%93161Leggett198121Lee200399-177">[174]</a></sup>

Within the party was established a [Political Bureau](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Politburo_of_the_Communist_Party_of_the_Soviet_Union "Politburo of the Communist Party of the Soviet Union") (Politburo) and [Organisation Bureau](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orgburo "Orgburo") (Orgburo) to accompany the existing [Central Committee](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_Committee_of_the_Communist_Party_of_the_Soviet_Union "Central Committee of the Communist Party of the Soviet Union"); the decisions of these party bodies had to be adopted by Sovnarkom and the [Council of Labour and Defence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Council_of_Labour_and_Defence "Council of Labour and Defence").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEService2000388Lee200398_178-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEService2000388Lee200398-178">[175]</a></sup> Lenin was the most significant figure in this governance structure as well as being the Chairman of Sovnarkom and sitting on the Council of Labour and Defence, and on the Central Committee and Politburo of the Communist Party.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEService2000388_179-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEService2000388-179">[176]</a></sup> The only individual to have anywhere near this influence was Lenin's right-hand man, [Yakov Sverdlov](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yakov_Sverdlov "Yakov Sverdlov"), who died in March 1919 during a [flu pandemic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1918_flu_pandemic "1918 flu pandemic").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERigby1979168,_170Service2000388_180-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTERigby1979168,_170Service2000388-180">[177]</a></sup> In November 1917, Lenin and his wife took a two-room flat within the Smolny Institute; the following month they left for a brief holiday in Halila, Finland.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEService2000325–326,_333Read2005211–212_181-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEService2000325%E2%80%93326,_333Read2005211%E2%80%93212-181">[178]</a></sup> In January 1918, he survived an assassination attempt in Petrograd; [Fritz Platten](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fritz_Platten "Fritz Platten"), who was with Lenin at the time, shielded him and was injured by a bullet.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShub1966361Pipes1990548Volkogonov1994229Service2000335–336Read2005198_182-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShub1966361Pipes1990548Volkogonov1994229Service2000335%E2%80%93336Read2005198-182">[179]</a></sup>

Concerned that the German Army posed a threat to Petrograd, in March 1918 Sovnarkom relocated to Moscow, initially as a temporary measure.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964156Shub1966350Pipes1990594Volkogonov1994185Service2000344Read2005212_183-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964156Shub1966350Pipes1990594Volkogonov1994185Service2000344Read2005212-183">[180]</a></sup> There, Lenin, Trotsky, and other Bolshevik leaders moved into the [Kremlin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kremlin "Kremlin"), where Lenin lived with his wife and sister Maria in a first-floor apartment adjacent to the room in which the Sovnarkom meetings were held.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964320–321Shub1966377Pipes199094–595Volkogonov1994187–188Service2000346–347Read2005212_184-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964320%E2%80%93321Shub1966377Pipes199094%E2%80%93595Volkogonov1994187%E2%80%93188Service2000346%E2%80%93347Read2005212-184">[181]</a></sup> Lenin disliked Moscow,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEService2000345_185-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEService2000345-185">[182]</a></sup> but rarely left the city centre during the rest of his life.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964466Service2000348_186-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964466Service2000348-186">[183]</a></sup> He survived a second assassination attempt, in Moscow in August 1918; he was shot following a public speech and injured badly.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964280Shub1966361–362Pipes1990806–807Volkogonov1994219–221Service2000367–368White2001155_187-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964280Shub1966361%E2%80%93362Pipes1990806%E2%80%93807Volkogonov1994219%E2%80%93221Service2000367%E2%80%93368White2001155-187">[184]</a></sup> A Socialist-Revolutionary, [Fanny Kaplan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fanny_Kaplan "Fanny Kaplan"), was arrested and executed.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964282–283Shub1966362–363Pipes1990807,_809Volkogonov1994222–228White2001155_188-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964282%E2%80%93283Shub1966362%E2%80%93363Pipes1990807,_809Volkogonov1994222%E2%80%93228White2001155-188">[185]</a></sup> The attack was widely covered in the Russian press, generating much sympathy for Lenin and boosting his popularity.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1994222,_231_189-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1994222,_231-189">[186]</a></sup> As a respite, he was driven in September 1918 to the luxurious [Gorki estate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gorki_Leninskiye "Gorki Leninskiye"), just outside Moscow, recently nationalized for him by the government.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEService2000369_190-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEService2000369-190">[187]</a></sup>

### Social, legal, and economic reform: 1917–1918

> To All Workers, Soldiers and Peasants. The Soviet authority will at once propose a democratic peace to all nations and an immediate armistice on all fronts. It will safeguard the transfer without compensation of all land—landlord, imperial, and monastery—to the peasants' committees; it will defend the soldiers' rights, introducing a complete democratisation of the army; it will establish workers' control over industry; it will ensure the convocation of the Constituent Assembly on the date set; it will supply the cities with bread and the villages with articles of first necessity; and it will secure to all nationalities inhabiting Russia the right of self-determination ... Long live the revolution!

—Lenin's political programme, October 1917<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERice1990161_191-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTERice1990161-191">[188]</a></sup>

Upon taking power, Lenin's regime issued a series of decrees. The first was a [Decree on Land](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decree_on_Land "Decree on Land"), which declared that the [landed estates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Landed_estate "Landed estate") of the aristocracy and the Orthodox Church should be nationalised and redistributed to peasants by local governments. This contrasted with Lenin's desire for [agricultural collectivisation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Agricultural_collectivisation "Agricultural collectivisation") but provided governmental recognition of the widespread peasant land seizures that had already occurred.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964252–253Pipes1990499Volkogonov1994341Service2000316–317White2001149Read2005194–195_192-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964252%E2%80%93253Pipes1990499Volkogonov1994341Service2000316%E2%80%93317White2001149Read2005194%E2%80%93195-192">[189]</a></sup> In November 1917, the government issued the Decree on the Press that closed many opposition media outlets deemed counter revolutionary. They claimed the measure would be temporary; the decree was widely criticised, including by many Bolsheviks, for compromising [freedom of the press](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freedom_of_the_press "Freedom of the press").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShub1966310Leggett19815–6,_8,_306Pipes1990521–522Service2000317–318White2001153Read2005235–236_193-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShub1966310Leggett19815%E2%80%936,_8,_306Pipes1990521%E2%80%93522Service2000317%E2%80%93318White2001153Read2005235%E2%80%93236-193">[190]</a></sup>

In November 1917, Lenin issued the [Declaration of the Rights of the Peoples of Russia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Declaration_of_the_Rights_of_the_Peoples_of_Russia "Declaration of the Rights of the Peoples of Russia"), which stated that non-Russian ethnic groups living inside the Republic had the right to secede from Russian authority and establish their own independent nation-states.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964249Pipes1990514Service2000321_194-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964249Pipes1990514Service2000321-194">[191]</a></sup> Many nations declared independence ([Finland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Finnish_Declaration_of_Independence "Finnish Declaration of Independence") and [Lithuania in December 1917](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Act_of_Independence_of_Lithuania "Act of Independence of Lithuania"), Latvia and Ukraine in January 1918, [Estonia in February 1918](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Estonian_Declaration_of_Independence "Estonian Declaration of Independence"), [Transcaucasia in April 1918](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transcaucasian_Democratic_Federative_Republic "Transcaucasian Democratic Federative Republic"), and [Poland in November 1918](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Polish_Republic "Second Polish Republic")).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964249Pipes1990514Read2005219_195-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964249Pipes1990514Read2005219-195">[192]</a></sup> Soon, the Bolsheviks actively promoted communist parties in these independent nation-states,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWhite2001159–160_196-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWhite2001159%E2%80%93160-196">[193]</a></sup> while at the Fifth All-Russian Congress of the Soviets in July 1918 a constitution was approved that reformed the Russian Republic into the [Russian Soviet Federative Socialist Republic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Soviet_Federative_Socialist_Republic "Russian Soviet Federative Socialist Republic").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964249_197-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964249-197">[194]</a></sup> Seeking to modernise the country, the government officially converted Russia from the [Julian calendar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Julian_calendar "Julian calendar") to the [Gregorian calendar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gregorian_calendar "Gregorian calendar") used in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESandle199984Read2005211_198-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTESandle199984Read2005211-198">[195]</a></sup>

In November 1917, Sovnarkom issued a decree abolishing Russia's legal system, calling on the use of "revolutionary conscience" to replace the abolished laws.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeggett1981172–173Pipes1990796–797Read2005242_199-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeggett1981172%E2%80%93173Pipes1990796%E2%80%93797Read2005242-199">[196]</a></sup> The courts were replaced by a two-tier system, namely the [Revolutionary Tribunals](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Revolutionary_tribunal_(Russia) "Revolutionary tribunal (Russia)") to deal with counter-revolutionary crimes,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeggett1981172Pipes1990798–799Ryan2012121_200-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeggett1981172Pipes1990798%E2%80%93799Ryan2012121-200">[197]</a></sup> and the [People's Courts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/People%27s_Court_(Soviet_Union) "People's Court (Soviet Union)") to deal with civil and other criminal offences. They were instructed to ignore pre-existing laws and base their rulings on the Sovnarkom decrees and a "socialist sense of justice."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHazard1965270Leggett1981172Pipes1990796–797_201-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHazard1965270Leggett1981172Pipes1990796%E2%80%93797-201">[198]</a></sup> November also saw an overhaul of the armed forces; Sovnarkom implemented [egalitarian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Egalitarian "Egalitarian") measures, abolished previous ranks, titles, and medals, and called on soldiers to establish committees to elect their commanders.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1994170_202-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1994170-202">[199]</a></sup>

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Dyadya_lenin.jpg/170px-Dyadya_lenin.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Dyadya_lenin.jpg)

Bolshevik propaganda poster from 1920, with a [political cartoon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Political_cartoon "Political cartoon") depicting Lenin sweeping away monarchs, clergy, and capitalists. The caption reads "Comrade Lenin Cleanses the Earth of Filth".

In October 1917, Lenin issued a decree limiting work for everyone in Russia to eight hours per day.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEService2000321_203-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEService2000321-203">[200]</a></sup> He also issued the Decree on Popular Education that stipulated that the government would guarantee free, secular education for all children in Russia,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEService2000321_203-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEService2000321-203">[200]</a></sup> and a decree establishing a system of state orphanages.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964260–261_204-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964260%E2%80%93261-204">[201]</a></sup> To combat mass illiteracy, a [literacy campaign](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Likbez "Likbez") was initiated; an estimated 5 million people enrolled in crash courses of basic literacy from 1920 to 1926.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESandle1999174_205-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTESandle1999174-205">[202]</a></sup> Embracing the equality of the sexes, laws were introduced that helped to emancipate women, by giving them economic autonomy from their husbands and removing restrictions on divorce.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964554–555Sandle199983_206-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964554%E2%80%93555Sandle199983-206">[203]</a></sup> [Zhenotdel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zhenotdel "Zhenotdel"), a Bolshevik women's organisation, was established to further these aims. <sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESandle1999122–123_207-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTESandle1999122%E2%80%93123-207">[204]</a></sup> Under Lenin, Russia became the first country to legalize abortion on demand in the first trimester.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavid1974417_208-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavid1974417-208">[205]</a></sup> Militantly atheist, Lenin and the Communist Party wanted to demolish organised religion.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964552Leggett1981308Sandle1999126Read2005238–239Ryan2012176,_182_209-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964552Leggett1981308Sandle1999126Read2005238%E2%80%93239Ryan2012176,_182-209">[206]</a></sup> In January 1918, the government decreed the separation of church and state, and prohibited religious instruction in schools.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1994373Leggett1981308Ryan2012177_210-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1994373Leggett1981308Ryan2012177-210">[207]</a></sup>

In November 1917, Lenin issued the Decree on Workers' Control, which called on the workers of each enterprise to establish an elected committee to monitor their enterprise's management.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPipes1990709Service2000321_211-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPipes1990709Service2000321-211">[208]</a></sup> That month they also issued an order requisitioning the country's gold,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1994171_212-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1994171-212">[209]</a></sup> and nationalised the banks, which Lenin saw as a major step toward socialism.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERigby197945–46Pipes1990682,_683Service2000321White2001153_213-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTERigby197945%E2%80%9346Pipes1990682,_683Service2000321White2001153-213">[210]</a></sup> In December, Sovnarkom established a [Supreme Council of the National Economy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supreme_Council_of_the_National_Economy "Supreme Council of the National Economy") (VSNKh), which had authority over industry, banking, agriculture, and trade.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERigby197950Pipes1990689Sandle199964Service2000321Read2005231_214-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTERigby197950Pipes1990689Sandle199964Service2000321Read2005231-214">[211]</a></sup> The factory committees were subordinate to the trade unions, which were subordinate to VSNKh; the state's centralised economic plan was prioritised over the workers' local economic interests.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964437–438Pipes1990709Sandle199964,_68_215-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964437%E2%80%93438Pipes1990709Sandle199964,_68-215">[212]</a></sup> In early 1918, Sovnarkom cancelled all foreign debts and refused to pay interest owed on them.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964263–264Pipes1990672_216-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964263%E2%80%93264Pipes1990672-216">[213]</a></sup> In April 1918, it nationalised foreign trade, establishing a state monopoly on imports and exports.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964264_217-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964264-217">[214]</a></sup> In June 1918, it decreed nationalisation of public utilities, railways, engineering, textiles, metallurgy, and mining, although often these were state-owned in name only.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPipes1990681,_692–693Sandle199996–97_218-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPipes1990681,_692%E2%80%93693Sandle199996%E2%80%9397-218">[215]</a></sup> Full-scale nationalisation did not take place until November 1920, when small-scale industrial enterprises were brought under state control.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPipes1990692–693Sandle199997_219-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPipes1990692%E2%80%93693Sandle199997-219">[216]</a></sup>

A faction of the Bolsheviks known as the "[Left Communists](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Left_Bolsheviks "Left Bolsheviks")" criticised Sovnarkom's economic policy as too moderate; they wanted nationalisation of all industry, agriculture, trade, finance, transport, and communication.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964236Service2000351–352_220-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964236Service2000351%E2%80%93352-220">[217]</a></sup> Lenin believed that this was impractical at that stage and that the government should only nationalise Russia's large-scale capitalist enterprises, such as the banks, railways, larger landed estates, and larger factories and mines, allowing smaller businesses to operate privately until they grew large enough to be successfully nationalised.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964236Service2000351–352_220-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964236Service2000351%E2%80%93352-220">[217]</a></sup> Lenin also disagreed with the Left Communists about the economic organisation; in June 1918, he argued that centralised economic control of industry was needed, whereas Left Communists wanted each factory to be controlled by its workers, a [syndicalist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Syndicalist "Syndicalist") approach that Lenin considered detrimental to the cause of socialism.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964259,_444–445_221-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964259,_444%E2%80%93445-221">[218]</a></sup>

Adopting a [left-libertarian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Left-libertarian "Left-libertarian") perspective, both the Left Communists and other factions in the Communist Party critiqued the decline of democratic institutions in Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESandle1999120_222-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTESandle1999120-222">[219]</a></sup> Internationally, many socialists decried Lenin's regime and denied that he was establishing socialism; in particular, they highlighted the lack of widespread political participation, popular consultation, and industrial democracy.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEService2000354–355_223-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEService2000354%E2%80%93355-223">[220]</a></sup> In late 1918, the Czech-Austrian Marxist [Karl Kautsky](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Kautsky "Karl Kautsky") authored an [anti-Leninist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-Leninist "Anti-Leninist") pamphlet condemning the anti-democratic nature of Soviet Russia, to which Lenin published a vociferous reply, _[The Proletarian Revolution and the Renegade Kautsky](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Proletarian_Revolution_and_the_Renegade_Kautsky "The Proletarian Revolution and the Renegade Kautsky")_.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964307–308Volkogonov1994178–179White2001156Read2005252–253Ryan2012123–124_224-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964307%E2%80%93308Volkogonov1994178%E2%80%93179White2001156Read2005252%E2%80%93253Ryan2012123%E2%80%93124-224">[221]</a></sup> German Marxist [Rosa Luxemburg](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rosa_Luxemburg "Rosa Luxemburg") echoed Kautsky's views,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShub1966329–330Service2000385White2001156Read2005253–254Ryan2012125_225-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShub1966329%E2%80%93330Service2000385White2001156Read2005253%E2%80%93254Ryan2012125-225">[222]</a></sup> while Russian [anarchist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anarchist "Anarchist") [Peter Kropotkin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peter_Kropotkin "Peter Kropotkin") described the Bolshevik seizure of power as "the burial of the Russian Revolution."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShub1966383_226-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShub1966383-226">[223]</a></sup>

### Treaty of Brest-Litovsk: 1917–1918

> \[By prolonging the war\] we unusually strengthen German imperialism, and the peace will have to be concluded anyway, but then the peace will be worse because it will be concluded by someone other than ourselves. No doubt the peace which we are now being forced to conclude is an indecent peace, but if war commences our government will be swept away and the peace will be concluded by another government.

—Lenin on peace with the Central Powers<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964193–194_227-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964193%E2%80%93194-227">[224]</a></sup>

Upon taking power, Lenin believed that a key policy of his government must be to withdraw from the First World War by establishing an armistice with the [Central Powers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_Powers "Central Powers") of Germany and Austria-Hungary.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShub1966331Pipes1990567_228-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShub1966331Pipes1990567-228">[225]</a></sup> He believed that ongoing war would create resentment among war-weary Russian troops, to whom he had promised peace, and that these troops and the advancing German Army threatened both his own government and the cause of international socialism.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964151Pipes1990567Service2000338_229-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964151Pipes1990567Service2000338-229">[226]</a></sup> By contrast, other Bolsheviks, in particular [Nikolai Bukharin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nikolai_Bukharin "Nikolai Bukharin") and the Left Communists, believed that peace with the Central Powers would be a betrayal of international socialism and that Russia should instead wage "a war of revolutionary defence" that would provoke an uprising of the German proletariat against their own government.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964190–191Shub1966337Pipes1990567Rice1990166_230-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964190%E2%80%93191Shub1966337Pipes1990567Rice1990166-230">[227]</a></sup>

Lenin proposed a three-month armistice in his [Decree on Peace](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decree_on_Peace "Decree on Peace") of November 1917, which was approved by the [Second Congress of Soviets](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Congress_of_Soviets "Second Congress of Soviets") and presented to the German and Austro-Hungarian governments.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964151–152Pipes1990571–572_231-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964151%E2%80%93152Pipes1990571%E2%80%93572-231">[228]</a></sup> The Germans responded positively, viewing this as an opportunity to focus on the [Western Front](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Western_Front_(World_War_I) "Western Front (World War I)") and stave off looming defeat.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964154Pipes1990572Rice1990166_232-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964154Pipes1990572Rice1990166-232">[229]</a></sup> In November, armistice talks began at [Brest-Litovsk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brest-Litovsk "Brest-Litovsk"), the headquarters of the German high command on the [Eastern Front](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_Front_(World_War_I) "Eastern Front (World War I)"), with the Russian delegation being led by Trotsky and [Adolph Joffe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adolph_Joffe "Adolph Joffe").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964161Shub1966331Pipes1990576_233-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964161Shub1966331Pipes1990576-233">[230]</a></sup> Meanwhile, a ceasefire until January was agreed.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964162–163Pipes1990576_234-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964162%E2%80%93163Pipes1990576-234">[231]</a></sup> During negotiations, the Germans insisted on keeping their wartime conquests, which included Poland, Lithuania, and [Courland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Courland "Courland"), whereas the Russians countered that this was a violation of these nations' rights to self-determination.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964171–172,_200–202Pipes1990578_235-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964171%E2%80%93172,_200%E2%80%93202Pipes1990578-235">[232]</a></sup> Some Bolsheviks had expressed hopes of dragging out negotiations until proletarian revolution broke out throughout Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERice1990166Service2000338_236-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTERice1990166Service2000338-236">[233]</a></sup> On 7 January 1918, Trotsky returned from Brest-Litovsk to St. Petersburg with an ultimatum from the Central Powers: either Russia accept Germany's territorial demands or the war would resume.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEService2000338_237-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEService2000338-237">[234]</a></sup>

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-R92623%2C_Brest-Litowsk%2C_Waffenstillstandsabkommen.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-R92623%2C_Brest-Litowsk%2C_Waffenstillstandsabkommen.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-R92623,_Brest-Litowsk,_Waffenstillstandsabkommen.jpg)

Signing of the armistice between Russia and Germany on 15 December 1917

In January and again in February, Lenin urged the Bolsheviks to accept Germany's proposals. He argued that the territorial losses were acceptable if it ensured the survival of the Bolshevik-led government. The majority of Bolsheviks rejected his position, hoping to prolong the armistice and call Germany's bluff.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964195Shub1966334,_337Service2000338–339,_340Read2005199_238-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964195Shub1966334,_337Service2000338%E2%80%93339,_340Read2005199-238">[235]</a></sup> On 18 February, the German Army launched [Operation Faustschlag](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Faustschlag "Operation Faustschlag"), advancing further into Russian-controlled territory and conquering [Dvinsk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dvinsk "Dvinsk") within a day.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964206,_209Shub1966337Pipes1990586–587Service2000340–341_239-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964206,_209Shub1966337Pipes1990586%E2%80%93587Service2000340%E2%80%93341-239">[236]</a></sup> At this point, Lenin finally convinced a small majority of the Bolshevik Central Committee to accept the Central Powers' demands.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPipes1990587Rice1990166–167Service2000341Read2005199_240-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPipes1990587Rice1990166%E2%80%93167Service2000341Read2005199-240">[237]</a></sup> On 23 February, the Central Powers issued a new ultimatum: Russia had to recognise German control not only of Poland and the Baltic states but also of Ukraine or face a full-scale invasion.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShub1966338Pipes1990592–593Service2000341_241-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShub1966338Pipes1990592%E2%80%93593Service2000341-241">[238]</a></sup>

On 3 March, the [Treaty of Brest-Litovsk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_Brest-Litovsk "Treaty of Brest-Litovsk") was signed.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964211–212Shub1966339Pipes1990595Rice1990167Service2000342White2001158–159_242-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964211%E2%80%93212Shub1966339Pipes1990595Rice1990167Service2000342White2001158%E2%80%93159-242">[239]</a></sup> It resulted in massive territorial losses for Russia, with 26% of the former Empire's population, 37% of its agricultural harvest area, 28% of its industry, 26% of its railway tracks, and three-quarters of its coal and iron deposits being transferred to German control.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPipes1990595Service2000342_243-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPipes1990595Service2000342-243">[240]</a></sup> Accordingly, the Treaty was deeply unpopular across Russia's political spectrum,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964213–214Pipes1990596–597_244-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964213%E2%80%93214Pipes1990596%E2%80%93597-244">[241]</a></sup> and several Bolsheviks and Left Socialist-Revolutionaries resigned from Sovnarkom in protest.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEService2000344_245-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEService2000344-245">[242]</a></sup> After the Treaty, Sovnarkom focused on trying to foment proletarian revolution in Germany, issuing an array of anti-war and anti-government publications in the country; the German government retaliated by expelling Russia's diplomats.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964313–314Shub1966387–388Pipes1990667–668Volkogonov1994193–194Service2000384_246-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964313%E2%80%93314Shub1966387%E2%80%93388Pipes1990667%E2%80%93668Volkogonov1994193%E2%80%93194Service2000384-246">[243]</a></sup> The Treaty nevertheless failed to stop the Central Powers' defeat; in November 1918, the German Emperor [Wilhelm II abdicated](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abdication_of_Wilhelm_II "Abdication of Wilhelm II") and the country's new administration signed the [Armistice](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Armistice_of_11_November_1918 "Armistice of 11 November 1918") with the [Allies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_I "Allies of World War I"). As a result, Sovnarkom proclaimed the Treaty of Brest-Litovsk void.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964303–304Pipes1990668Volkogonov1994194Service2000384_247-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964303%E2%80%93304Pipes1990668Volkogonov1994194Service2000384-247">[244]</a></sup>

### Anti-Kulak campaigns, Cheka, and Red Terror: 1918–1922

> \[The bourgeoisie\] practised terror _against the workers, soldiers and peasants_ in the interests of a small group of landowners and bankers, whereas the Soviet regime applies decisive measures against landowners, plunderers and their accomplices _in the interests of the workers, soldiers and peasants_.

—Lenin on the Red Terror<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1994182_248-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1994182-248">[245]</a></sup>

By early 1918, many cities in western Russia faced famine as a result of chronic food shortages.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964236Pipes1990558,_723Rice1990170Volkogonov1994190_249-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964236Pipes1990558,_723Rice1990170Volkogonov1994190-249">[246]</a></sup> Lenin blamed this on the [kulaks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kulaks "Kulaks"), or wealthier peasants, who allegedly hoarded the grain that they had produced to increase its financial value. In May 1918, he issued a requisitioning order that established armed detachments to confiscate grain from kulaks for distribution in the cities, and in June called for the formation of [Committees of Poor Peasants](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Committees_of_Poor_Peasants "Committees of Poor Peasants") to aid in requisitioning.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964236–237Shub1966353Pipes1990560,_722,_732–736Rice1990170Volkogonov1994181,_342–343Service2000349,_358–359White2001164Read2005218_250-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964236%E2%80%93237Shub1966353Pipes1990560,_722,_732%E2%80%93736Rice1990170Volkogonov1994181,_342%E2%80%93343Service2000349,_358%E2%80%93359White2001164Read2005218-250">[247]</a></sup> This policy resulted in vast social disorder and violence, as armed detachments often clashed with peasant groups, helping to set the stage for the civil war.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964254Pipes1990728,_734–736Volkogonov1994197Ryan2012105_251-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964254Pipes1990728,_734%E2%80%93736Volkogonov1994197Ryan2012105-251">[248]</a></sup> A prominent example of Lenin's views was his [August 1918 telegram to the Bolsheviks of Penza](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lenin%27s_Hanging_Order "Lenin's Hanging Order"), which called upon them to suppress a peasant insurrection by publicly hanging at least 100 "known kulaks, rich men, \[and\] bloodsuckers."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964277–278Pipes1990737Service2000365White2001155–156Ryan2012106_252-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964277%E2%80%93278Pipes1990737Service2000365White2001155%E2%80%93156Ryan2012106-252">[249]</a></sup>

The requisitions disincentivised peasants from producing more grain than they could personally consume, and thus production slumped.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964450Pipes1990726_253-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964450Pipes1990726-253">[250]</a></sup> A booming [black market](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Black_market "Black market") supplemented the official state-sanctioned economy,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPipes1990700–702Lee2003100_254-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPipes1990700%E2%80%93702Lee2003100-254">[251]</a></sup> and Lenin called on [speculators](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Speculators "Speculators"), black marketeers and [looters](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Looters "Looters") to be shot.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964195Pipes1990794Volkogonov1994181Read2005249_255-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964195Pipes1990794Volkogonov1994181Read2005249-255">[252]</a></sup> Both the Socialist-Revolutionaries and Left Socialist-Revolutionaries condemned the armed appropriations of grain at the Fifth All-Russian Congress of Soviets in July 1918.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964237_256-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964237-256">[253]</a></sup> Realising that the Committees of the Poor Peasants were also persecuting peasants who were not kulaks and thus contributing to anti-government feeling among the peasantry, in December 1918 Lenin abolished them.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEService2000385White2001164Read2005218_257-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEService2000385White2001164Read2005218-257">[254]</a></sup>

Lenin repeatedly emphasised the need for terror and violence in overthrowing the old order and ensuring the success of the revolution.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShub1966344Pipes1990790–791Volkogonov1994181,_196Read2005247–248_258-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShub1966344Pipes1990790%E2%80%93791Volkogonov1994181,_196Read2005247%E2%80%93248-258">[255]</a></sup> Speaking to the [All-Russian Central Executive Committee](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/All-Russian_Central_Executive_Committee "All-Russian Central Executive Committee") of the Soviets in November 1917, he declared that "the state is an institution built up for the sake of exercising violence. Previously, this violence was exercised by a handful of moneybags over the entire people; now we want \[...\] to organise violence in the interests of the people."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShub1966312_259-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShub1966312-259">[256]</a></sup> He strongly opposed suggestions to abolish capital punishment.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964435–436_260-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964435%E2%80%93436-260">[257]</a></sup> Fearing anti-Bolshevik forces would overthrow his administration, in December 1917 Lenin ordered the establishment of the [Emergency Commission for Combating Counter-Revolution and Sabotage](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cheka "Cheka"), or Cheka, a political police force led by [Felix Dzerzhinsky](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Felix_Dzerzhinsky "Felix Dzerzhinsky").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShub1966345–347Rigby197920–21Pipes1990800Volkogonov1994233Service2000321–322White2001153Read2005186,_208–209_261-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShub1966345%E2%80%93347Rigby197920%E2%80%9321Pipes1990800Volkogonov1994233Service2000321%E2%80%93322White2001153Read2005186,_208%E2%80%93209-261">[258]</a></sup>

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Lenin_Krupskaya_and_Ulyanova_in_car_at_Red_Army_parade_full_photo_19180501.jpg/220px-Lenin_Krupskaya_and_Ulyanova_in_car_at_Red_Army_parade_full_photo_19180501.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Lenin_Krupskaya_and_Ulyanova_in_car_at_Red_Army_parade_full_photo_19180501.jpg)

Lenin with his wife and sister in a car at a Red Army parade at [Khodynka Field](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khodynka_Field "Khodynka Field") in Moscow, [May Day](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/May_Day "May Day") 1918

In September 1918, Sovnarkom passed a decree that inaugurated the [Red Terror](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_Terror "Red Terror"), a system of repression orchestrated by the [Cheka](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cheka "Cheka") secret police.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeggett1981174Volkogonov1994233–234Sandle1999112Ryan2012111_262-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeggett1981174Volkogonov1994233%E2%80%93234Sandle1999112Ryan2012111-262">[259]</a></sup> Although sometimes described as an attempt to eliminate the entire bourgeoisie,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShub1966366Sandle1999112_263-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShub1966366Sandle1999112-263">[260]</a></sup> Lenin did not want to exterminate all members of this class, merely those who sought to reinstate their rule.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERyan2012116_264-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTERyan2012116-264">[261]</a></sup> The majority of the Terror's victims were well-to-do citizens or former members of the Tsarist administration;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPipes1990821Ryan2012114–115_265-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPipes1990821Ryan2012114%E2%80%93115-265">[262]</a></sup> others were non-bourgeois anti-Bolsheviks and perceived social undesirables such as prostitutes.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShub1966366Sandle1999113Read2005210Ryan2012114–115_266-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShub1966366Sandle1999113Read2005210Ryan2012114%E2%80%93115-266">[263]</a></sup> The Cheka claimed the right to both sentence and execute anyone whom it deemed to be an enemy of the government, without recourse to the Revolutionary Tribunals.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeggett1981173–174Pipes1990801_267-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeggett1981173%E2%80%93174Pipes1990801-267">[264]</a></sup> Accordingly, throughout Soviet Russia the Cheka carried out killings, often in large numbers.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeggett1981199–200Pipes1990819–820Ryan2012107_268-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeggett1981199%E2%80%93200Pipes1990819%E2%80%93820Ryan2012107-268">[265]</a></sup> For example, the Petrograd Cheka executed 512 people in a few days.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShub1966364Ryan2012114_269-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShub1966364Ryan2012114-269">[266]</a></sup> There are no surviving records to provide an accurate figure of how many perished in the Red Terror;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPipes1990837_270-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPipes1990837-270">[267]</a></sup> later estimates of historians have ranged between 10,000 and 15,000,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERyan2012114_271-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTERyan2012114-271">[268]</a></sup> and 50,000 to 140,000.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPipes1990834_272-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPipes1990834-272">[269]</a></sup>

Lenin never witnessed this violence or participated in it first-hand,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1994202Read2005247_273-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1994202Read2005247-273">[270]</a></sup> and publicly distanced himself from it.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPipes1990796_274-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPipes1990796-274">[271]</a></sup> His published articles and speeches rarely called for executions, but he regularly did so in his coded telegrams and confidential notes.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1994202_275-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1994202-275">[272]</a></sup> Many Bolsheviks expressed disapproval of the Cheka's mass executions and feared the organisation's apparent unaccountability.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPipes1990825Ryan2012117,_120_276-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPipes1990825Ryan2012117,_120-276">[273]</a></sup> The Communist Party tried to restrain its activities in February 1919, stripping it of its powers of tribunal and execution in those areas not under official [martial law](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Martial_law "Martial law"), but the Cheka continued as before in swathes of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeggett1981174–175,_183Pipes1990828–829Ryan2012121_277-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeggett1981174%E2%80%93175,_183Pipes1990828%E2%80%93829Ryan2012121-277">[274]</a></sup> By 1920, the Cheka had become the most powerful institution in Soviet Russia, exerting influence over all other state apparatus.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPipes1990829–830,_832_278-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPipes1990829%E2%80%93830,_832-278">[275]</a></sup>

A decree in April 1919 resulted in the establishment of [concentration camps](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Concentration_camps "Concentration camps"), which were entrusted to the Cheka,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeggett1981176–177Pipes1990832,_834_279-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeggett1981176%E2%80%93177Pipes1990832,_834-279">[276]</a></sup> later administered by a new government agency, [Gulag](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gulag "Gulag").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPipes1990835Volkogonov1994235_280-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPipes1990835Volkogonov1994235-280">[277]</a></sup> By the end of 1920, 84 camps had been established across Soviet Russia, holding about 50,000 prisoners; by October 1923, this had grown to 315 camps and about 70,000 inmates.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeggett1981178Pipes1990836_281-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeggett1981178Pipes1990836-281">[278]</a></sup> Those interned in the camps were used as [slave labour](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Slave_labour "Slave labour").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeggett1981176Pipes1990832–833_282-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeggett1981176Pipes1990832%E2%80%93833-282">[279]</a></sup> From July 1922, intellectuals deemed to be opposing the Bolshevik government were exiled to inhospitable regions or deported from Russia altogether; Lenin personally scrutinised the lists of those to be dealt with in this manner.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1994358–360Ryan2012172–173,_175–176_283-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1994358%E2%80%93360Ryan2012172%E2%80%93173,_175%E2%80%93176-283">[280]</a></sup> In May 1922, Lenin issued a decree calling for the execution of anti-Bolshevik priests, causing between 14,000 and 20,000 deaths.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1994376–377Read2005239Ryan2012179_284-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1994376%E2%80%93377Read2005239Ryan2012179-284">[281]</a></sup> The Russian Orthodox Church was worst affected; the government's anti-religious policies also harmed [Roman Catholic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_Catholic "Roman Catholic") and [Protestant](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protestant "Protestant") churches, [Jewish](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jewish "Jewish") synagogues, and [Islamic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic "Islamic") mosques.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1994381_285-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1994381-285">[282]</a></sup>

### Civil War and the Polish–Soviet War: 1918–1920

> The existence of the Soviet Republic alongside the imperialist states over the long run is unthinkable. In the end, either the one or the other will triumph. And until that end will have arrived, a series of the most terrible conflicts between the Soviet Republic and the bourgeois governments is unavoidable. This means that the ruling class, the proletariat, if it only wishes to rule and is to rule, must demonstrate this also with its military organization.

—Lenin on war<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPipes1990610_286-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPipes1990610-286">[283]</a></sup>

Lenin expected Russia's aristocracy and bourgeoisie to oppose his government, but he believed that the numerical superiority of the lower classes, coupled with the Bolsheviks' ability to effectively organise them, guaranteed a swift victory in any conflict.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEService2000357_287-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEService2000357-287">[284]</a></sup> In this, he failed to anticipate the intensity of the violent opposition to Bolshevik rule in Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEService2000357_287-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEService2000357-287">[284]</a></sup> A long and bloody [Civil War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Civil_War "Russian Civil War") ensued between the Bolshevik [Reds](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_Army "Red Army") and the anti-Bolshevik [Whites](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/White_movement "White movement"), starting in 1917 and ending in 1923 with the Reds' victory. It also encompassed ethnic conflicts on Russia's borders, and anti-Bolshevik [peasant](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tambov_Rebellion "Tambov Rebellion") and [left-wing uprisings](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Left-wing_uprisings_against_the_Bolsheviks "Left-wing uprisings against the Bolsheviks") throughout the former Empire.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEService2000391–392_288-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEService2000391%E2%80%93392-288">[285]</a></sup> Accordingly, various historians have seen the civil war as representing two distinct conflicts: one between the revolutionaries and the counterrevolutionaries, and the other between different revolutionary factions.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELee200384,_88_289-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTELee200384,_88-289">[286]</a></sup>

The White armies were established by former Tsarist military officers,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERead2005205_290-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTERead2005205-290">[287]</a></sup> and included [Anton Denikin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anton_Denikin "Anton Denikin")'s [Volunteer Army](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Volunteer_Army "Volunteer Army") in [South Russia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Russia_(1919%E2%80%931920) "South Russia (1919–1920)"),<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShub1966355Leggett1981204Rice1990173,_175Volkogonov1994198Service2000357,_382Read2005187_291-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShub1966355Leggett1981204Rice1990173,_175Volkogonov1994198Service2000357,_382Read2005187-291">[288]</a></sup> [Alexander Kolchak](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_Kolchak "Alexander Kolchak")'s forces in Siberia,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964334,_343,_357Leggett1981204Service2000382,_392Read2005205–206_292-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964334,_343,_357Leggett1981204Service2000382,_392Read2005205%E2%80%93206-292">[289]</a></sup> and [Nikolai Yudenich](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nikolai_Yudenich "Nikolai Yudenich")'s troops in the newly independent Baltic states.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeggett1981204Read2005206_293-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeggett1981204Read2005206-293">[290]</a></sup> The Whites were bolstered when 35,000 members of the [Czech Legion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Czech_Legion "Czech Legion"), who were [prisoners of war](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prisoners_of_war "Prisoners of war") from the conflict with the Central Powers, turned against Sovnarkom and allied with the [Committee of Members of the Constituent Assembly](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Committee_of_Members_of_the_Constituent_Assembly "Committee of Members of the Constituent Assembly") (Komuch), an anti-Bolshevik government established in Samara.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964288–289Pipes1990624–630Service2000360White2001161–162Read2005205_294-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964288%E2%80%93289Pipes1990624%E2%80%93630Service2000360White2001161%E2%80%93162Read2005205-294">[291]</a></sup> The Whites were also backed by Western governments who perceived the Treaty of Brest-Litovsk as a betrayal of the Allied war effort and feared the Bolsheviks' calls for world revolution.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964262–263_295-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964262%E2%80%93263-295">[292]</a></sup> In 1918, Great Britain, France, United States, Canada, Italy, and Serbia landed 10,000 troops in [Murmansk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Murmansk "Murmansk"), seizing [Kandalaksha](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kandalaksha "Kandalaksha"), while later that year British, American, and Japanese forces landed in [Vladivostok](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladivostok "Vladivostok").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964291Shub1966354_296-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964291Shub1966354-296">[293]</a></sup> Western troops soon pulled out of the civil war, instead only supporting the Whites with officers, technicians and armaments, but Japan remained because they saw the conflict as an opportunity for territorial expansion.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964331,_333_297-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964331,_333-297">[294]</a></sup>
