Lenin tasked Trotsky with establishing a [Workers' and Peasants' Red Army](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Workers%27_and_Peasants%27_Red_Army "Workers' and Peasants' Red Army"), and with his support, Trotsky organised a [Revolutionary Military Council](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Revolutionary_Military_Council "Revolutionary Military Council") in September 1918, remaining its chairman until 1925.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPipes1990610,_612Volkogonov1994198_298-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPipes1990610,_612Volkogonov1994198-298">[295]</a></sup> Recognising their valuable military experience, Lenin agreed that officers from the old Tsarist army could serve in the Red Army, although Trotsky established military councils to monitor their activities.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964337Pipes1990609,_612,_629Volkogonov1994198Service2000383Read2005217_299-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964337Pipes1990609,_612,_629Volkogonov1994198Service2000383Read2005217-299">[296]</a></sup> The Reds held control of Russia's two largest cities, Moscow and Petrograd, as well as most of [Great Russia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Russia "Great Russia"), while the Whites were located largely on the former Empire's peripheries.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964248,_262_300-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964248,_262-300">[297]</a></sup> The latter were therefore hindered by being both fragmented and geographically scattered,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPipes1990651Volkogonov1994200White2001162Lee200381_301-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPipes1990651Volkogonov1994200White2001162Lee200381-301">[298]</a></sup> and because their ethnic Russian supremacism alienated the region's national minorities.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964251White2001163Read2005220_302-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964251White2001163Read2005220-302">[299]</a></sup> Anti-Bolshevik armies carried out the [White Terror](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/White_Terror_(Russia) "White Terror (Russia)"), a campaign of violence against perceived Bolshevik supporters which was typically more spontaneous than the state-sanctioned Red Terror.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeggett1981201Pipes1990792Volkogonov1994202–203Read2005250_303-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeggett1981201Pipes1990792Volkogonov1994202%E2%80%93203Read2005250-303">[300]</a></sup> Both White and Red Armies were responsible for attacks against Jewish communities, prompting Lenin to issue a condemnation of [antisemitism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antisemitism "Antisemitism"), blaming prejudice against Jews on [capitalist propaganda](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Capitalist_propaganda "Capitalist propaganda").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeggett1981201Volkogonov1994203–204_304-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeggett1981201Volkogonov1994203%E2%80%93204-304">[301]</a></sup>

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/VictimOfInternational.jpg/220px-VictimOfInternational.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:VictimOfInternational.jpg)

[White](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/White_movement "White movement") anti-Bolshevik propaganda poster, in which Lenin is depicted in a red robe aiding other Bolsheviks in sacrificing Russia to a statue of Marx, c. 1918–1919

In July 1918, Sverdlov informed Sovnarkom that the Ural Regional Soviet had overseen the [murder of the former Tsar and his immediate family](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Murder_of_the_Romanov_family "Murder of the Romanov family") in [Yekaterinburg](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yekaterinburg "Yekaterinburg") to prevent them from being rescued by advancing White troops.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShub1966357–358Pipes1990781–782Volkogonov1994206–207Service2000364–365_305-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShub1966357%E2%80%93358Pipes1990781%E2%80%93782Volkogonov1994206%E2%80%93207Service2000364%E2%80%93365-305">[302]</a></sup> Although lacking proof, biographers and historians like [Richard Pipes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Richard_Pipes "Richard Pipes") and [Dmitri Volkogonov](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dmitri_Volkogonov "Dmitri Volkogonov") have expressed the view that the killing was probably sanctioned by Lenin;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPipes1990763,_770–771Volkogonov1994211_306-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPipes1990763,_770%E2%80%93771Volkogonov1994211-306">[303]</a></sup> conversely, historian James Ryan cautioned that there was "no reason" to believe this.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERyan2012109_307-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTERyan2012109-307">[304]</a></sup> Whether Lenin sanctioned it or not, he still regarded it as necessary, highlighting the precedent set by the [execution of Louis XVI](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Execution_of_Louis_XVI "Execution of Louis XVI") in the [French Revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/French_Revolution "French Revolution").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1994208_308-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1994208-308">[305]</a></sup>

After the Brest-Litovsk Treaty, the Left Socialist-Revolutionaries had abandoned the coalition and increasingly viewed the Bolsheviks as traitors to the revolution.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPipes1990635_309-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPipes1990635-309">[306]</a></sup> In July 1918, the Left Socialist-Revolutionary [Yakov Blumkin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yakov_Blumkin "Yakov Blumkin") assassinated the German ambassador to Russia, [Wilhelm von Mirbach](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wilhelm_von_Mirbach "Wilhelm von Mirbach"), hoping that the ensuing diplomatic incident would lead to a relaunched revolutionary war against Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964244Shub1966355Pipes1990636–640Service2000360–361White2001159Read2005199_310-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964244Shub1966355Pipes1990636%E2%80%93640Service2000360%E2%80%93361White2001159Read2005199-310">[307]</a></sup> The Left Socialist-Revolutionaries then [launched a coup in Moscow](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Left_SR_uprising "Left SR uprising"), shelling the Kremlin and seizing the city's central post office before being stopped by Trotsky's forces.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964242Pipes1990642–644Read2005250_311-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964242Pipes1990642%E2%80%93644Read2005250-311">[308]</a></sup> The party's leaders and many members were arrested and imprisoned but were treated more leniently than other opponents of the Bolsheviks.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964244Pipes1990644Volkogonov1994172_312-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964244Pipes1990644Volkogonov1994172-312">[309]</a></sup>

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Polish-soviet_propaganda_poster_1920.jpg/220px-Polish-soviet_propaganda_poster_1920.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Polish-soviet_propaganda_poster_1920.jpg)

Bolshevik [anti-Polish](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-Polish_sentiment "Anti-Polish sentiment") propaganda poster, 1920

By 1919, the White armies were in retreat and by the start of 1920 were defeated on all three fronts.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeggett1981184Service2000402Read2005206_313-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeggett1981184Service2000402Read2005206-313">[310]</a></sup> Although Sovnarkom were victorious, the territorial extent of the Russian state had been reduced, for many non-Russian ethnic groups had used the disarray to push for national independence.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHall201583_314-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHall201583-314">[311]</a></sup> In March 1921, during [a related war against Poland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Soviet_War "Polish–Soviet War"), the [Peace of Riga](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peace_of_Riga "Peace of Riga") was signed, splitting disputed territories in [Belarus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Belarusian_Democratic_Republic "Belarusian Democratic Republic") and [Ukraine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ukrainian_People%27s_Republic "Ukrainian People's Republic") between the [Republic of Poland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Polish_Republic "Second Polish Republic") and [Soviet Russia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Russia "Soviet Russia"). Soviet Russia sought to re-conquer all newly [independent nations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pro-independence_movements_in_the_Russian_Civil_War "Pro-independence movements in the Russian Civil War") of the former Empire, although their success was limited. [Estonia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Estonian_War_of_Independence "Estonian War of Independence"), [Finland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Finnish_Civil_War "Finnish Civil War"), [Latvia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Latvian_War_of_Independence "Latvian War of Independence"), and [Lithuania](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lithuanian%E2%80%93Soviet_War "Lithuanian–Soviet War") all repelled Soviet invasions, while [Ukraine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ukrainian%E2%80%93Soviet_War "Ukrainian–Soviet War"), Belarus (as a result of the [Polish–Soviet War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Soviet_War "Polish–Soviet War")), [Armenia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_Army_invasion_of_Armenia "Red Army invasion of Armenia"), [Azerbaijan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_Army_invasion_of_Azerbaijan "Red Army invasion of Azerbaijan") and [Georgia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_Army_invasion_of_Georgia "Red Army invasion of Georgia") were occupied by the Red Army.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELee200384,_88_289-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTELee200384,_88-289">[286]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoldstein201350_315-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoldstein201350-315">[312]</a></sup> By 1921, Soviet Russia had defeated the Ukrainian national movements and occupied the [Caucasus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caucasus "Caucasus"), although [anti-Bolshevik uprisings](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Basmachi_movement "Basmachi movement") in [Central Asia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_Asia "Central Asia") lasted until the late 1920s.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHall201584_316-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHall201584-316">[313]</a></sup>

After the German [Ober Ost](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ober_Ost "Ober Ost") garrisons were withdrawn from the Eastern Front following the Armistice, [both Soviet Russian armies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_westward_offensive_of_1918%E2%80%931919 "Soviet westward offensive of 1918–1919") and Polish ones moved in to fill the vacuum.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavies200326–27_317-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies200326%E2%80%9327-317">[314]</a></sup> The newly independent Polish state and the Soviet government each sought territorial expansion in the region.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavies200327–30_318-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies200327%E2%80%9330-318">[315]</a></sup> Polish and Russian troops first clashed in February 1919,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavies200322,_27_319-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies200322,_27-319">[316]</a></sup> with the conflict developing into the [Polish–Soviet War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Soviet_War "Polish–Soviet War").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964389Rice1990182Volkogonov1994281Service2000407White2001161Davies200329–30_320-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964389Rice1990182Volkogonov1994281Service2000407White2001161Davies200329%E2%80%9330-320">[317]</a></sup> Unlike the Soviets' previous conflicts, this had greater implications for the export of revolution and the future of Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavies200322_321-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies200322-321">[318]</a></sup> Polish forces pushed into Ukraine and by May 1920 [had taken Kiev](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kiev_offensive_(1920) "Kiev offensive (1920)") from the Soviets.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964389Rice1990182Volkogonov1994281Service2000407White2001161_322-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964389Rice1990182Volkogonov1994281Service2000407White2001161-322">[319]</a></sup> After forcing the [Polish Army](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish_Army "Polish Army") back, Lenin urged the Red Army to invade Poland itself, believing that the Polish proletariat would rise up to support the Russian troops and thus spark European revolution. Trotsky and other Bolsheviks were sceptical, but agreed to the invasion. The Polish proletariat did not rise, and the Red Army was defeated at the [Battle of Warsaw](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Warsaw_(1920) "Battle of Warsaw (1920)").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964391–395Shub1966396Rice1990182–183Service2000408–409,_412White2001161_323-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964391%E2%80%93395Shub1966396Rice1990182%E2%80%93183Service2000408%E2%80%93409,_412White2001161-323">[320]</a></sup> The Polish armies pushed the Red Army back into Russia, forcing Sovnarkom to sue for peace; the war culminated in the [Peace of Riga](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peace_of_Riga "Peace of Riga"), in which Russia ceded territory to Poland.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERice1990183Volkogonov1994388Service2000412_324-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTERice1990183Volkogonov1994388Service2000412-324">[321]</a></sup>

### Comintern and world revolution: 1919–1920

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/%D0%9B%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BD_%D0%92._%D0%98._1919_%D0%B3%D0%BE%D0%B4.jpg/220px-%D0%9B%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BD_%D0%92._%D0%98._1919_%D0%B3%D0%BE%D0%B4.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:%D0%9B%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BD_%D0%92._%D0%98._1919_%D0%B3%D0%BE%D0%B4.jpg)

Lenin speaking in Moscow's [Red Square](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_Square "Red Square") on May Day 1919

After the Armistice on the Western Front, Lenin believed that the breakout of the European revolution was imminent.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShub1966387Rice1990173_325-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShub1966387Rice1990173-325">[322]</a></sup> Seeking to promote this, Sovnarkom supported the establishment of [Béla Kun](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/B%C3%A9la_Kun "Béla Kun")'s [soviet government in Hungary](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hungarian_Soviet_Republic "Hungarian Soviet Republic") in March 1919, followed by the [soviet government in Bavaria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bavarian_Council_Republic "Bavarian Council Republic") and [various revolutionary socialist uprisings](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Revolutions_of_1917%E2%80%9323 "Revolutions of 1917–23") in other parts of Germany, including [that of the Spartacus League](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spartacist_uprising "Spartacist uprising").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964333Shub1966388Rice1990173Volkogonov1994395_326-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964333Shub1966388Rice1990173Volkogonov1994395-326">[323]</a></sup> During Russia's Civil War, the Red Army was sent into the newly independent national republics on Russia's borders to aid Marxists there in establishing soviet systems of government.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEService2000385–386_327-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEService2000385%E2%80%93386-327">[324]</a></sup> In Europe, this resulted in the creation of new communist-led states in [Estonia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Commune_of_the_Working_People_of_Estonia "Commune of the Working People of Estonia"), [Latvia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Latvian_Socialist_Soviet_Republic "Latvian Socialist Soviet Republic"), [Lithuania](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lithuanian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic_(1918%E2%80%9319) "Lithuanian Soviet Socialist Republic (1918–19)"), [Belarus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Socialist_Soviet_Republic_of_Byelorussia "Socialist Soviet Republic of Byelorussia"), and [Ukraine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ukrainian_Soviet_Republic "Ukrainian Soviet Republic"), all of which were nominally independent from Russia but in fact controlled from Moscow,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEService2000385–386_327-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEService2000385%E2%80%93386-327">[324]</a></sup> while further east it led to the creation of communist governments in [Outer Mongolia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mongolian_People%27s_Republic "Mongolian People's Republic").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964531,_536_328-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964531,_536-328">[325]</a></sup> Various senior Bolsheviks wanted these absorbed into the Russian state; Lenin insisted that national sensibilities should be respected, but reassured his comrades that these nations' new Communist Party administrations were under the _de facto_ authority of Sovnarkom.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEService2000386_329-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEService2000386-329">[326]</a></sup>

In late 1918, the [British Labour Party](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/British_Labour_Party "British Labour Party") called for the establishment of an international conference of socialist parties, the [Labour and Socialist International](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Labour_and_Socialist_International "Labour and Socialist International").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShub1966389–390_330-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShub1966389%E2%80%93390-330">[327]</a></sup> Lenin saw this as a revival of the Second International, which he had despised, and formulated his own rival international socialist conference to offset its impact.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShub1966390_331-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShub1966390-331">[328]</a></sup> Organised with the aid of Zinoviev, [Nikolai Bukharin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nikolai_Bukharin "Nikolai Bukharin"), Trotsky, [Christian Rakovsky](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christian_Rakovsky "Christian Rakovsky"), and [Angelica Balabanoff](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Angelica_Balabanoff "Angelica Balabanoff"),<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShub1966390_331-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShub1966390-331">[328]</a></sup> the [First Congress](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1st_Congress_of_the_Comintern "1st Congress of the Comintern") of this [Communist International](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communist_International "Communist International") (Comintern) opened in Moscow in March 1919.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964525Shub1966390Rice1990174Volkogonov1994390Service2000386White2001160Read2005225_332-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964525Shub1966390Rice1990174Volkogonov1994390Service2000386White2001160Read2005225-332">[329]</a></sup> It lacked global coverage; most of the delegates resided within the countries of the former Russian Empire, and most of the international delegates were not recognised by any socialist parties in their own nations.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964525Shub1966390–391Rice1990174Service2000386White2001160_333-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964525Shub1966390%E2%80%93391Rice1990174Service2000386White2001160-333">[330]</a></sup> Accordingly, the Bolsheviks dominated proceedings,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEService2000387White2001160_334-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEService2000387White2001160-334">[331]</a></sup> with Lenin subsequently authoring a series of regulations that meant that only socialist parties endorsing the Bolsheviks' views were permitted to join Comintern.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964525Shub1966398Read2005225–226_335-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964525Shub1966398Read2005225%E2%80%93226-335">[332]</a></sup> During the first conference, Lenin spoke to the delegates, lambasting the parliamentary path to socialism espoused by revisionist Marxists like Kautsky and repeating his calls for a violent overthrow of Europe's bourgeoisie governments.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEService2000387_336-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEService2000387-336">[333]</a></sup> While Zinoviev became Comintern's president, Lenin retained significant influence over it.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShub1966395Volkogonov1994391_337-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShub1966395Volkogonov1994391-337">[334]</a></sup>

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/V._I._Lenin_in_one_of_the_committees_of_the_II_Congress_of_the_Comintern.jpg/220px-V._I._Lenin_in_one_of_the_committees_of_the_II_Congress_of_the_Comintern.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:V._I._Lenin_in_one_of_the_committees_of_the_II_Congress_of_the_Comintern.jpg)

Lenin in one of the committees of the II Congress of the Comintern

The [Second Congress of the Communist International](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Congress_of_the_Communist_International "Second Congress of the Communist International") opened in Petrograd's [Smolny Institute](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Smolny_Institute "Smolny Institute") in July 1920, representing the last time that Lenin visited a city other than Moscow.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShub1966397Service2000409_338-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShub1966397Service2000409-338">[335]</a></sup> There, he encouraged foreign delegates to emulate the Bolsheviks' seizure of power and abandoned his longstanding viewpoint that capitalism was a necessary stage in societal development, instead, encouraging those nations under colonial occupation to transform their pre-capitalist societies directly into socialist ones.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEService2000409–410_339-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEService2000409%E2%80%93410-339">[336]</a></sup> For this conference, he authored _["Left-Wing" Communism: An Infantile Disorder](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/%22Left-Wing%22_Communism:_An_Infantile_Disorder ""Left-Wing" Communism: An Infantile Disorder")_, a short book articulating his criticism of elements within the British and German communist parties who refused to enter their nations' parliamentary systems and trade unions; instead, he urged them to do so to advance the revolutionary cause.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964415–420White2001161,_180–181_340-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964415%E2%80%93420White2001161,_180%E2%80%93181-340">[337]</a></sup> The conference had to be suspended for several days due to the ongoing war with Poland,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEService2000410_341-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEService2000410-341">[338]</a></sup> and was relocated to Moscow, where it continued to hold sessions until August.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShub1966397_342-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShub1966397-342">[339]</a></sup> Lenin's predicted world revolution did not materialise, as the Hungarian communist government was overthrown, and the German Marxist uprisings suppressed.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964341Shub1966396Rice1990174_343-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964341Shub1966396Rice1990174-343">[340]</a></sup>

### Famine and the New Economic Policy: 1920–1922

Within the Communist Party, there was dissent from two factions, the [Group of Democratic Centralism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Group_of_Democratic_Centralism "Group of Democratic Centralism") and the [Workers' Opposition](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Workers%27_Opposition "Workers' Opposition"), both of which accused the Russian state of being too centralised and bureaucratic.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964437–438Shub1966406Rice1990183Service2000419White2001167–168_344-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964437%E2%80%93438Shub1966406Rice1990183Service2000419White2001167%E2%80%93168-344">[341]</a></sup> The Workers' Opposition, which had connections to the official state trade unions, also expressed the concern that the government had lost the trust of the Russian working class.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShub1966406Service2000419White2001167_345-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShub1966406Service2000419White2001167-345">[342]</a></sup> They were angered by Trotsky's suggestion that the trade unions be eliminated. He deemed the unions to be superfluous in a "[workers' state](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Workers%27_state "Workers' state")", but Lenin disagreed, believing it best to retain them; most Bolsheviks embraced Lenin's view in the 'trade union discussion'.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964436,_442Rice1990183–184Sandle1999104–105Service2000422–423White2001168Read2005269_346-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964436,_442Rice1990183%E2%80%93184Sandle1999104%E2%80%93105Service2000422%E2%80%93423White2001168Read2005269-346">[343]</a></sup> To deal with the dissent, at the [Tenth Party Congress](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/10th_Congress_of_the_Russian_Communist_Party_(Bolsheviks) "10th Congress of the Russian Communist Party (Bolsheviks)") in February 1921, Lenin introduced a ban on factional activity within the party, under pain of expulsion.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWhite2001170_347-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWhite2001170-347">[344]</a></sup>

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Victims_of_the_1921_famine_in_Russia.jpg/220px-Victims_of_the_1921_famine_in_Russia.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Victims_of_the_1921_famine_in_Russia.jpg)

Victims of the famine in [Buzuluk, Orenburg Oblast](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Buzuluk,_Orenburg_Oblast "Buzuluk, Orenburg Oblast"), winter 1921/1922

Caused in part by a drought, the [Russian famine of 1921](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_famine_of_1921 "Russian famine of 1921") was the most severe that the country had experienced since [that of 1891](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_famine_of_1891%E2%80%9392 "Russian famine of 1891–92"), resulting in around five million deaths.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERyan2012164_348-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTERyan2012164-348">[345]</a></sup> The famine was exacerbated by government requisitioning, as well as the export of large quantities of Russian grain.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1994343,_347_349-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1994343,_347-349">[346]</a></sup> To aid the famine victims, the US government [established](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Famine_Relief_Act "Russian Famine Relief Act") the [American Relief Administration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Relief_Administration "American Relief Administration") to distribute food;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964508Shub1966414Volkogonov1994345White2001172_350-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964508Shub1966414Volkogonov1994345White2001172-350">[347]</a></sup> Lenin was suspicious of this aid and had it closely monitored.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1994346_351-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1994346-351">[348]</a></sup> During the famine, [Patriarch Tikhon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Patriarch_Tikhon "Patriarch Tikhon") called on Orthodox churches to sell unnecessary items to help feed the starving, an action endorsed by the government.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1994374–375_352-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1994374%E2%80%93375-352">[349]</a></sup> In February 1922, Sovnarkom went further by calling on all valuables belonging to religious institutions to be [forcibly appropriated and sold](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1922_confiscation_of_Russian_Orthodox_Church_property "1922 confiscation of Russian Orthodox Church property").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1994375–376Read2005251Ryan2012176,_177_353-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1994375%E2%80%93376Read2005251Ryan2012176,_177-353">[350]</a></sup> Tikhon opposed the sale of items used within the [Eucharist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eucharist "Eucharist") and many clergy resisted the appropriations, resulting in violence.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1994376Ryan2012178_354-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1994376Ryan2012178-354">[351]</a></sup>

In 1920 and 1921, local opposition to requisitioning resulted in anti-Bolshevik peasant uprisings breaking out across Russia, which were suppressed.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964467Shub1966406Volkogonov1994343Service2000425White2001168Read2005220Ryan2012154_355-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964467Shub1966406Volkogonov1994343Service2000425White2001168Read2005220Ryan2012154-355">[352]</a></sup> Among the most significant was the [Tambov Rebellion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tambov_Rebellion "Tambov Rebellion"), which was put down by the Red Army.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964459Leggett1981330–333Service2000423–424White2001168Ryan2012154–155_356-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964459Leggett1981330%E2%80%93333Service2000423%E2%80%93424White2001168Ryan2012154%E2%80%93155-356">[353]</a></sup> In February 1921, workers went on strike in Petrograd, resulting in the government proclaiming martial law in the city and sending in the Red Army to quell demonstrations.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShub1966406–407Leggett1981324–325Rice1990184Read2005220Ryan2012170_357-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShub1966406%E2%80%93407Leggett1981324%E2%80%93325Rice1990184Read2005220Ryan2012170-357">[354]</a></sup> In March, the [Kronstadt rebellion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kronstadt_rebellion "Kronstadt rebellion") began when sailors in [Kronstadt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kronstadt "Kronstadt") revolted against the Bolshevik government, demanding that all socialists be allowed to publish freely, that independent trade unions be given freedom of assembly and that peasants be allowed free markets and not be subject to requisitioning. Lenin declared that the mutineers had been misled by the Socialist-Revolutionaries and foreign imperialists, calling for violent reprisals.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964469–470Shub1966405Leggett1981325–326Rice1990184Service2000427White2001169Ryan2012170_358-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964469%E2%80%93470Shub1966405Leggett1981325%E2%80%93326Rice1990184Service2000427White2001169Ryan2012170-358">[355]</a></sup> Under Trotsky's leadership, the Red Army put down the rebellion on 17 March, resulting in thousands of deaths and the internment of survivors in labour camps.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964470–471Shub1966408–409Leggett1981327–328Rice1990184–185Service2000427–428Ryan2012171–172_359-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964470%E2%80%93471Shub1966408%E2%80%93409Leggett1981327%E2%80%93328Rice1990184%E2%80%93185Service2000427%E2%80%93428Ryan2012171%E2%80%93172-359">[356]</a></sup>

> You must attempt first to build small bridges which shall lead to a land of small peasant holdings through State Capitalism to Socialism. Otherwise you will never lead tens of millions of people to Communism. This is what the objective forces of the development of the Revolution have taught.

—Lenin on the NEP, 1921<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShub1966412–413_360-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShub1966412%E2%80%93413-360">[357]</a></sup>

In February 1921, Lenin introduced a [New Economic Policy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Economic_Policy "New Economic Policy") (NEP) to the Politburo; he convinced most senior Bolsheviks of its necessity and it passed into law in April.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShub1966411Rice1990185Service2000421,_424–427,_429_361-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShub1966411Rice1990185Service2000421,_424%E2%80%93427,_429-361">[358]</a></sup> Lenin explained the policy in a booklet, _On the Food Tax_, in which he stated that the NEP represented a return to the original Bolshevik economic plans; he claimed that these had been derailed by the civil war, in which Sovnarkom had been forced to resort to the economic policies of [war communism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/War_communism "War communism"), which involved the nationalization of industry, centralized distribution of output, coercive or forced requisition of agricultural production, and attempts to eliminate money circulation, private enterprises and [free trade](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Free_trade "Free trade"), leading to the severe economic collapse.<sup id="cite_ref-gregory2004_362-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-gregory2004-362">[359]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964479–480Sandle1999155Service2000430White2001170,_171_363-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964479%E2%80%93480Sandle1999155Service2000430White2001170,_171-363">[360]</a></sup> The NEP allowed some private enterprise within Russia, permitting the reintroduction of the wage system and allowing peasants to sell produce on the open market while being taxed on their earnings.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShub1966411Sandle1999153,_158Service2000430White2001169Read2005264–265_364-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShub1966411Sandle1999153,_158Service2000430White2001169Read2005264%E2%80%93265-364">[361]</a></sup> The policy also allowed for a return to privately owned small industry; basic industry, transport and foreign trade remained under state control.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShub1966412Service2000430Read2005266Ryan2012159_365-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShub1966412Service2000430Read2005266Ryan2012159-365">[362]</a></sup> Lenin termed this "[state capitalism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_capitalism "State capitalism")",<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964479Shub1966412Sandle1999155Ryan2012159_366-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964479Shub1966412Sandle1999155Ryan2012159-366">[363]</a></sup> and many Bolsheviks thought it to be a betrayal of socialist principles.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESandle1999151Service2000422White2001171_367-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTESandle1999151Service2000422White2001171-367">[364]</a></sup> Lenin biographers have often characterised the introduction of the NEP as one of his most significant achievements, and some believe that had it not been implemented then Sovnarkom would have been quickly overthrown by popular uprisings.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEService2000421,_434_368-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEService2000421,_434-368">[365]</a></sup>

In January 1920, the government brought in universal labour conscription, ensuring that all citizens aged between 16 and 50 had to work.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPipes1990703–707Sandle1999103Ryan2012143_369-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPipes1990703%E2%80%93707Sandle1999103Ryan2012143-369">[366]</a></sup> Lenin also called for a mass [electrification](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electrification "Electrification") project of Russia, the [GOELRO plan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/GOELRO_plan "GOELRO plan"), which began in February 1920; Lenin's declaration that "communism is Soviet power plus the electrification of the whole country" was widely cited in later years.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964423,_582Sandle1999107White2001165Read2005230_370-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964423,_582Sandle1999107White2001165Read2005230-370">[367]</a></sup> Seeking to advance the Russian economy through foreign trade, Sovnarkom sent delegates to the [Genoa Conference](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genoa_Conference "Genoa Conference"); Lenin had hoped to attend but was prevented by ill health.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964567–569_371-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964567%E2%80%93569-371">[368]</a></sup> The conference resulted in a [Russian agreement with Germany](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_Rapallo_(1922) "Treaty of Rapallo (1922)"), which followed on from an earlier [trade agreement with the United Kingdom](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anglo-Soviet_Trade_Agreement "Anglo-Soviet Trade Agreement").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964574,_576–577Service2000432,_441_372-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964574,_576%E2%80%93577Service2000432,_441-372">[369]</a></sup> Lenin hoped that by allowing foreign corporations to invest in Russia, Sovnarkom would exacerbate rivalries between the capitalist nations and hasten their downfall; he tried to rent the oil fields of [Kamchatka](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kamchatka "Kamchatka") to an American corporation to heighten tensions between the US and Japan, who desired Kamchatka for their empire.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964424–427_373-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964424%E2%80%93427-373">[370]</a></sup>

### Declining health and conflict with Stalin: 1920–1923

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/%D0%9B%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BD_%D0%B2_%D0%93%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%85_%281923%29.jpg/220px-%D0%9B%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BD_%D0%B2_%D0%93%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%85_%281923%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:%D0%9B%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BD_%D0%B2_%D0%93%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%85_(1923).jpg)

Lenin in a wheelchair shortly after his third stroke in March 1923

To Lenin's embarrassment and horror, in April 1920 the Bolsheviks held a large party to celebrate his 50th birthday, which was also marked by widespread celebrations across Russia and the publication of poems and biographies dedicated to him.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964414Rice1990177–178Service2000405Read2005260–261_374-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964414Rice1990177%E2%80%93178Service2000405Read2005260%E2%80%93261-374">[371]</a></sup> Between 1920 and 1926, twenty volumes of Lenin's _Collected Works_ were published; some material was omitted.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1994283_375-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1994283-375">[372]</a></sup> During 1920, several prominent Western figures visited Lenin in Russia; these included the author [H. G. Wells](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/H._G._Wells "H. G. Wells") and the philosopher [Bertrand Russell](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bertrand_Russell "Bertrand Russell"),<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964404–409Rice1990178–179Service2000440_376-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964404%E2%80%93409Rice1990178%E2%80%93179Service2000440-376">[373]</a></sup> as well as the anarchists [Emma Goldman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emma_Goldman "Emma Goldman") and [Alexander Berkman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_Berkman "Alexander Berkman").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964409–411_377-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964409%E2%80%93411-377">[374]</a></sup> Lenin was also visited at the Kremlin by [Armand](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inessa_Armand "Inessa Armand"), who was in increasingly poor health.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964433–434Shub1966380–381Rice1990181Service2000414–415Read2005258_378-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964433%E2%80%93434Shub1966380%E2%80%93381Rice1990181Service2000414%E2%80%93415Read2005258-378">[375]</a></sup> He sent her to a sanatorium in [Kislovodsk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kislovodsk "Kislovodsk") in the Northern Caucasus to recover, but she died there in September 1920 during a [cholera](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cholera "Cholera") epidemic.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964434Shub1966381–382Rice1990181Service2000415Read2005258_379-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964434Shub1966381%E2%80%93382Rice1990181Service2000415Read2005258-379">[376]</a></sup> Her body was transported to Moscow, where a visibly grief-stricken Lenin oversaw her burial beneath the Kremlin Wall.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERice1990181–182Service2000416–417Read2005258_380-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTERice1990181%E2%80%93182Service2000416%E2%80%93417Read2005258-380">[377]</a></sup>

Lenin became seriously ill by the latter half of 1921,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShub1966426Lewin196933Rice1990187Volkogonov1994409Service2000435_381-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShub1966426Lewin196933Rice1990187Volkogonov1994409Service2000435-381">[378]</a></sup> experiencing [hyperacusis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hyperacusis "Hyperacusis"), [insomnia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Insomnia "Insomnia"), and regular headaches.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShub1966426Rice1990187Service2000435_382-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShub1966426Rice1990187Service2000435-382">[379]</a></sup> At the Politburo's insistence, in July he left Moscow for a month's leave at his Gorki mansion, where he was cared for by his wife and sister.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEService2000436Read2005281Rice1990187_383-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEService2000436Read2005281Rice1990187-383">[380]</a></sup> Lenin began to contemplate the possibility of suicide, asking both Krupskaya and Stalin to acquire [potassium cyanide](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Potassium_cyanide "Potassium cyanide") for him.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1994420,_425–426Service2000439Read2005280,_282_384-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1994420,_425%E2%80%93426Service2000439Read2005280,_282-384">[381]</a></sup> Twenty-six physicians were hired to help Lenin during his final years; many of them were foreign and had been hired at great expense.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1994443Service2000437_385-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1994443Service2000437-385">[382]</a></sup> Some suggested that his sickness could have been caused by metal [oxidation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oxidation "Oxidation") from the [bullets](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bullet "Bullet") that were lodged in his body from the 1918 assassination attempt; in April 1922 he underwent a surgical operation to successfully remove them.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964598–599Shub1966426Service2000443White2001172Read2005258_386-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964598%E2%80%93599Shub1966426Service2000443White2001172Read2005258-386">[383]</a></sup> The symptoms continued after this, with Lenin's doctors unsure of the cause; some suggested that he had [neurasthenia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neurasthenia "Neurasthenia") or [cerebral arteriosclerosis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cerebral_arteriosclerosis "Cerebral arteriosclerosis"). In May 1922, he had his first stroke, temporarily losing his ability to speak and being paralysed on his right side.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964600Shub1966426–427Lewin196933Service2000443White2001173Read2005258_387-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964600Shub1966426%E2%80%93427Lewin196933Service2000443White2001173Read2005258-387">[384]</a></sup> He convalesced at Gorki and had largely recovered by July.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShub1966427–428Service2000446_388-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShub1966427%E2%80%93428Service2000446-388">[385]</a></sup> In October, he returned to Moscow; in December, he had a second stroke and returned to Gorki.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964634Shub1966431–432Lewin196933–34White2001173_389-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964634Shub1966431%E2%80%93432Lewin196933%E2%80%9334White2001173-389">[386]</a></sup>

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/LeninDistrictMO_Gorki_estate_05-2017_img2.jpg/220px-LeninDistrictMO_Gorki_estate_05-2017_img2.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:LeninDistrictMO_Gorki_estate_05-2017_img2.jpg)

Lenin's Gorki mansion, where he spent much of his final years (_pictured in 2017_)

Despite his illness, Lenin remained keenly interested in political developments. When the Socialist Revolutionary Party's leadership was found guilty of conspiring against the government in a trial held between June and August 1922, Lenin called for their execution; they were instead imprisoned indefinitely, only being executed during the [Great Purge](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Purge "Great Purge") of Stalin's leadership.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964600–602Shub1966428–430Leggett1981318Sandle1999164Service2000442–443Read2005269Ryan2012174–175_390-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964600%E2%80%93602Shub1966428%E2%80%93430Leggett1981318Sandle1999164Service2000442%E2%80%93443Read2005269Ryan2012174%E2%80%93175-390">[387]</a></sup> With Lenin's support, the government also succeeded in virtually eradicating Menshevism in Russia by expelling all Mensheviks from state institutions and enterprises in March 1923 and then imprisoning the party's membership in concentration camps.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1994310Leggett1981320–322Aves1996175–178Sandle1999164Lee2003103–104Ryan2012172_391-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1994310Leggett1981320%E2%80%93322Aves1996175%E2%80%93178Sandle1999164Lee2003103%E2%80%93104Ryan2012172-391">[388]</a></sup> Lenin was concerned by the survival of the Tsarist bureaucratic system in Soviet Russia,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewin19698–9White2001176Read2005270–272_392-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewin19698%E2%80%939White2001176Read2005270%E2%80%93272-392">[389]</a></sup> particularly during his final years.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964578Rice1990189_393-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964578Rice1990189-393">[390]</a></sup> Condemning bureaucratic attitudes, he suggested a total overhaul to deal with such problems,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERice1990192–193_394-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTERice1990192%E2%80%93193-394">[391]</a></sup> in one letter complaining that "we are being sucked into a foul bureaucratic swamp".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964578_395-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964578-395">[392]</a></sup>

During December 1922 and January 1923, Lenin dictated "[Lenin's Testament](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lenin%27s_Testament "Lenin's Testament")", in which he discussed the personal qualities of his comrades, particularly Trotsky and Stalin.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964638–639Shub1966433Lewin196973–75Volkogonov1994417Service2000464White2001173–174_396-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964638%E2%80%93639Shub1966433Lewin196973%E2%80%9375Volkogonov1994417Service2000464White2001173%E2%80%93174-396">[393]</a></sup> He recommended that Stalin be removed from the position of General Secretary of the Communist Party, deeming him ill-suited for the position.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964647Shub1966434–435Rice1990192Volkogonov1994273Service2000469White2001174–175Read2005278–279_397-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964647Shub1966434%E2%80%93435Rice1990192Volkogonov1994273Service2000469White2001174%E2%80%93175Read2005278%E2%80%93279-397">[394]</a></sup> Instead he recommended Trotsky for the job, describing him as "the most capable man in the present Central Committee"; he highlighted Trotsky's superior intellect but at the same time criticised his self-assurance and inclination toward excess administration.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964640Shub1966434–435Volkogonov1994249,_418Service2000465White2001174_398-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964640Shub1966434%E2%80%93435Volkogonov1994249,_418Service2000465White2001174-398">[395]</a></sup> During this period he dictated a criticism of the bureaucratic nature of the Workers' and Peasants' Inspectorate, calling for the recruitment of new, working-class staff as an antidote to this problem,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964666–667,_669Lewin1969120–121Service2000468Read2005273_399-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964666%E2%80%93667,_669Lewin1969120%E2%80%93121Service2000468Read2005273-399">[396]</a></sup> while in another article he called for the state to combat illiteracy, promote punctuality and conscientiousness within the populace, and encourage peasants to join co‑operatives.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964650–654Service2000470_400-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964650%E2%80%93654Service2000470-400">[397]</a></sup>

> Stalin is too crude, and this defect which is entirely acceptable in our milieu and in relationships among us as communists, becomes unacceptable in the position of General Secretary. I therefore propose to comrades that they should devise a means of removing him from this job and should appoint to this job someone else who is distinguished from comrade Stalin in all other respects only by the single superior aspect that he should be more tolerant, more polite and more attentive towards comrades, less capricious, etc.

—Lenin, 4 January 1923<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEService2000369_190-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEService2000369-190">[187]</a></sup>

In Lenin's absence, Stalin had begun consolidating his power both by appointing his supporters to prominent positions,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShub1966426,_434Lewin196934–35_401-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShub1966426,_434Lewin196934%E2%80%9335-401">[398]</a></sup> and by cultivating an image of himself as Lenin's closest intimate and deserving successor.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1994263–264_402-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1994263%E2%80%93264-402">[399]</a></sup> In December 1922, Stalin took responsibility for Lenin's regimen, being tasked by the Politburo with controlling who had access to him.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewin196970Rice1990191Volkogonov1994273,_416_403-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewin196970Rice1990191Volkogonov1994273,_416-403">[400]</a></sup> Lenin was increasingly critical of Stalin; while Lenin was insisting that the state should retain its monopoly on international trade during mid-1922, Stalin was leading other Bolsheviks in unsuccessfully opposing this.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964635Lewin196935–40Service2000451–452White2001173_404-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964635Lewin196935%E2%80%9340Service2000451%E2%80%93452White2001173-404">[401]</a></sup> There were personal arguments between the two as well; Stalin had upset Krupskaya by shouting at her during a phone conversation, which in turn greatly angered Lenin, who sent Stalin a letter expressing his annoyance.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964637–638,_669Shub1966435–436Lewin196971,_85,_101Volkogonov1994273–274,_422–423Service2000463,_472–473White2001173,_176Read2005279_405-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964637%E2%80%93638,_669Shub1966435%E2%80%93436Lewin196971,_85,_101Volkogonov1994273%E2%80%93274,_422%E2%80%93423Service2000463,_472%E2%80%93473White2001173,_176Read2005279-405">[402]</a></sup>

The most significant political division between the two emerged during the [Georgian Affair](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Georgian_Affair "Georgian Affair"). Stalin had suggested that both the [forcibly Sovietized](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_Army_invasion_of_Georgia "Red Army invasion of Georgia") Georgia and neighbouring countries like [Azerbaijan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_Army_invasion_of_Azerbaijan "Red Army invasion of Azerbaijan") and [Armenia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_Army_invasion_of_Armenia "Red Army invasion of Armenia"), which were all invaded and occupied by the Red Army, should be merged into the Russian state, despite the protestations of their local Soviet-installed governments.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964607–608Lewin196943–49Rice1990190–191Volkogonov1994421Service2000452,_453–455White2001175–176_406-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964607%E2%80%93608Lewin196943%E2%80%9349Rice1990190%E2%80%93191Volkogonov1994421Service2000452,_453%E2%80%93455White2001175%E2%80%93176-406">[403]</a></sup> Lenin saw this as an expression of Great Russian ethnic chauvinism by Stalin and his supporters, instead calling for these nation-states to join Russia as semi-independent parts of a greater union, which he suggested be called the Union of Soviet Republics of Europe and Asia.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964608Lewin196950Leggett1981354Volkogonov1994421Service2000455White2001175_407-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964608Lewin196950Leggett1981354Volkogonov1994421Service2000455White2001175-407">[404]</a></sup> After some resistance to the proposal, Stalin eventually accepted it but, with Lenin's agreement, he changed the name of the newly proposed state to "[Union of Soviet Socialist Republics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Union_of_Soviet_Socialist_Republics "Union of Soviet Socialist Republics") (USSR)".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEService2000455,_456_408-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEService2000455,_456-408">[405]</a></sup> Lenin sent Trotsky to speak on his behalf at a Central Committee plenum in December, where the plans for the Soviet Union were sanctioned; these plans were then ratified on 30 December by the Congress of Soviets, resulting in the formation of the Soviet Union.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewin196940,_99–100Volkogonov1994421Service2000460–461,_468_409-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewin196940,_99%E2%80%93100Volkogonov1994421Service2000460%E2%80%93461,_468-409">[406]</a></sup> Despite his poor health, Lenin was elected chairman of the new government of the Soviet Union.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERigby1979221_410-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTERigby1979221-410">[407]</a></sup>

## Political ideology

### Marxism and Leninism

> We do not pretend that Marx or Marxists know the road to socialism in all its concreteness. That is nonsense. We know the direction of the road, we know what class forces will lead it, but concretely, practically, this will be shown by _the experience of the millions_ when they undertake the act.

—Lenin, 11 September 1917<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964150_411-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964150-411">[408]</a></sup>

Lenin was a devout Marxist,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERyan201218_412-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTERyan201218-412">[409]</a></sup> and believed that his interpretation of Marxism, first termed "Leninism" by Martov in 1904,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1994409_413-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1994409-413">[410]</a></sup> was the sole authentic and orthodox one.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESandle199935Service2000237_414-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTESandle199935Service2000237-414">[411]</a></sup> According to his Marxist perspective, humanity would eventually reach pure communism, becoming a stateless, classless, egalitarian society of workers who were free from [exploitation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Exploitation_of_labour "Exploitation of labour") and [alienation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marx%27s_theory_of_alienation "Marx's theory of alienation"), controlled their own destiny, and abided by the rule "[from each according to his ability, to each according to his needs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/From_each_according_to_his_ability,_to_each_according_to_his_needs "From each according to his ability, to each according to his needs")."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESandle199941_415-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTESandle199941-415">[412]</a></sup> According to Volkogonov, Lenin "deeply and sincerely" believed that the path he was setting Russia on would ultimately lead to the establishment of this communist society.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1994206_416-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1994206-416">[413]</a></sup>

Lenin's Marxist beliefs led him to the view that society could not transform directly from its present state to communism, but must first enter a period of socialism, and so his main concern was how to convert Russia into a socialist society. To do so, he believed that a "dictatorship of the proletariat" was necessary to suppress the bourgeoisie and develop a socialist economy.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESandle199935_417-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTESandle199935-417">[414]</a></sup> He defined socialism as "an order of civilized co-operators in which the [means of production](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Means_of_production "Means of production") are socially owned",<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShub1966432_418-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShub1966432-418">[415]</a></sup> and believed that this economic system had to be expanded until it could create a [society of abundance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Post-scarcity_economy "Post-scarcity economy").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESandle199941_415-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTESandle199941-415">[412]</a></sup> To achieve this, he saw bringing the Russian economy under state control to be his central concern, with "all citizens" becoming "hired employees of the state" in his words.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESandle199942–43_419-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTESandle199942%E2%80%9343-419">[416]</a></sup> Lenin's interpretation of socialism was centralised, planned, and statist, with both production and distribution strictly controlled.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESandle199941_415-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTESandle199941-415">[412]</a></sup> He believed that all workers throughout the country would voluntarily join to enable the state's economic and political centralisation.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESandle199938_420-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTESandle199938-420">[417]</a></sup> In this way, his calls for "workers' control" of the means of production referred not to the direct control of enterprises by their workers, but the operation of all enterprises under the control of a "workers' state."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESandle199943–44,_63_421-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTESandle199943%E2%80%9344,_63-421">[418]</a></sup> This resulted in what some perceive as two conflicting themes within Lenin's thought: popular workers' control, and a centralised, hierarchical, coercive state apparatus.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESandle199936_422-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTESandle199936-422">[419]</a></sup>

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Lenin_1919-03-18.jpg/220px-Lenin_1919-03-18.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Lenin_1919-03-18.jpg)

Lenin speaking in 1919

Before 1914, Lenin's views were largely in accordance with mainstream European Marxist orthodoxy.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERyan201218_412-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTERyan201218-412">[409]</a></sup> Although he derided Marxists who adopted ideas from contemporary non-Marxist philosophers and sociologists,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEService2000203_423-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEService2000203-423">[420]</a></sup> his own ideas were influenced not only by Russian Marxist theory but also by wider ideas from the Russian revolutionary movement,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESandle199929White20011_424-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTESandle199929White20011-424">[421]</a></sup> including those of the Narodnik agrarian-socialists.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEService2000173_425-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEService2000173-425">[422]</a></sup> He adapted his ideas according to changing circumstances,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERyan201213_426-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTERyan201213-426">[423]</a></sup> including the pragmatic realities of governing Russia amid war, famine, and economic collapse.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESandle199957White2001151_427-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTESandle199957White2001151-427">[424]</a></sup> As Leninism developed, Lenin revised the established Marxist orthodoxy and introduced innovations in Marxist thought.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERyan201218_412-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTERyan201218-412">[409]</a></sup>

In his theoretical writings, particularly _[Imperialism, the Highest Stage of Capitalism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Imperialism,_the_Highest_Stage_of_Capitalism "Imperialism, the Highest Stage of Capitalism"),_ Lenin discussed what he regarded as developments in capitalism since Marx's death; in his view, it had reached the new stage of [state monopoly capitalism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_monopoly_capitalism "State monopoly capitalism").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESandle199934_428-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTESandle199934-428">[425]</a></sup> He believed that although Russia's economy was dominated by the peasantry, the presence of monopoly capitalism in Russia meant that the country was sufficiently materially developed to move to socialism.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWhite2001150–151_429-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWhite2001150%E2%80%93151-429">[426]</a></sup> Leninism adopted a more absolutist and doctrinaire perspective than other variants of Marxism,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERyan201218_412-3"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTERyan201218-412">[409]</a></sup> and distinguished itself by the emotional intensity of its [liberationist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emancipation "Emancipation") vision.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERyan201219_430-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTERyan201219-430">[427]</a></sup> It also stood out by emphasising the role of a vanguard who could lead the proletariat to revolution,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERyan201219_430-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTERyan201219-430">[427]</a></sup> and elevated the role of violence as a revolutionary instrument.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERyan20123_431-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTERyan20123-431">[428]</a></sup>

### Democracy and the national question

> \[Lenin\] accepted truth as handed down by Marx and selected data and arguments to bolster that truth. He did not question old Marxist scripture, he merely commented, and the comments have become a new scripture.

—Biographer [Louis Fischer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louis_Fischer "Louis Fischer"), 1964<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964213_432-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964213-432">[429]</a></sup>

Lenin believed that the [representative democracy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Representative_democracy "Representative democracy") of capitalist countries gave the illusion of democracy while maintaining the "dictatorship of the bourgeoisie"; describing the representative democratic system of the United States, he referred to the "spectacular and meaningless duels between two bourgeois parties", both of whom were led by "astute multimillionaires" that exploited the American proletariat.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERice1990121_433-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTERice1990121-433">[430]</a></sup> He opposed liberalism, exhibiting a general antipathy toward [liberty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Liberty "Liberty") as a value,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1994471_434-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1994471-434">[431]</a></sup> and believing that liberalism's freedoms were fraudulent because it did not free labourers from capitalist exploitation.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShub1966443_435-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShub1966443-435">[432]</a></sup>

Lenin declared that "Soviet government is many millions of times more democratic than the most democratic-bourgeois republic", the latter of which was simply "a democracy for the rich."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964310Shub1966442_436-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964310Shub1966442-436">[433]</a></sup> He regarded his "dictatorship of the proletariat" as democratic because, he claimed, it involved the election of representatives to the [soviets](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_(council) "Soviet (council)"), workers electing their own officials, and the regular rotation and involvement of all workers in the administration of the state.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESandle199936–37_437-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTESandle199936%E2%80%9337-437">[434]</a></sup> Lenin's belief as to what a proletariat state should look like nevertheless deviated from that adopted by the Marxist mainstream; European Marxists like Kautsky envisioned a democratically elected parliamentary government in which the proletariat had a majority, whereas Lenin called for a strong, centralised state apparatus that excluded any input from the bourgeois.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERyan201219_430-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTERyan201219-430">[427]</a></sup>

Lenin was an [internationalist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Internationalism_(politics) "Internationalism (politics)") and a keen supporter of [world revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_revolution "World revolution"), deeming national borders to be an outdated concept and nationalism a distraction from class struggle.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer196454Shub1966423Pipes1990352_438-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer196454Shub1966423Pipes1990352-438">[435]</a></sup> He believed that in a socialist society, the world's nations would inevitably merge and result in a single [world government](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_government "World government").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer196488–89_439-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer196488%E2%80%9389-439">[436]</a></sup> He believed that this socialist state would need to be a centralised, [unitary one](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unitary_state "Unitary state"), and regarded [federalism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federalism "Federalism") as a bourgeois concept.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer196487Montefiore2007266_440-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer196487Montefiore2007266-440">[437]</a></sup> In his writings, Lenin espoused [anti-imperialist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-imperialist "Anti-imperialist") ideas and stated that all nations deserved "the right of self-determination."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer196487_441-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer196487-441">[438]</a></sup> He supported [wars of national liberation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wars_of_national_liberation "Wars of national liberation"), accepting that such conflicts might be necessary for a minority group to break away from a [socialist state](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Socialist_state "Socialist state"), because socialist states are not "holy or insured against mistakes or weaknesses."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer196491,_93_442-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer196491,_93-442">[439]</a></sup>

Prior to taking power in 1917, he was concerned that ethnic and national minorities would make the Soviet state ungovernable with their calls for independence; according to the historian [Simon Sebag Montefiore](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Simon_Sebag_Montefiore "Simon Sebag Montefiore"), Lenin thus encouraged Stalin to develop "a theory that offered the ideal of autonomy and the right of secession without necessarily having to grant either."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMontefiore2007266_443-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMontefiore2007266-443">[440]</a></sup> On taking power, Lenin called for the dismantling of the bonds that had forced minority ethnic groups to remain in the Russian Empire and espoused their right to secede but also expected them to reunite immediately in the spirit of proletariat internationalism.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPage194817Page1950354_444-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPage194817Page1950354-444">[441]</a></sup> He was willing to use military force to ensure this unity, resulting in armed incursions into the independent states that formed in Ukraine, Georgia, Poland, Finland, and the Baltic states.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPage1950355_445-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPage1950355-445">[442]</a></sup> Only when its conflicts with Finland, the Baltic states, and Poland proved unsuccessful did Lenin's government officially recognise their independence.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPage1950342_446-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPage1950342-446">[443]</a></sup>

## Personal life and characteristics

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Lenin_Speech_in_May_1920.png/220px-Lenin_Speech_in_May_1920.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Lenin_Speech_in_May_1920.png)

Lenin speaking to a crowd in Moscow's [Sverdlov Square](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theatre_Square_(Moscow) "Theatre Square (Moscow)") with [Leon Trotsky](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky "Leon Trotsky") and [Lev Kamenev](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lev_Kamenev "Lev Kamenev") beside him, May 1920

Lenin saw himself as a man of destiny and firmly believed in the righteousness of his cause and his own ability as a revolutionary leader.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEService2000159,_202Read2005207_447-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEService2000159,_202Read2005207-447">[444]</a></sup> Biographer [Louis Fischer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louis_Fischer "Louis Fischer") described him as "a lover of radical change and maximum upheaval", a man for whom "there was never a middle-ground. He was an either-or, black-or-red exaggerator".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer196447,_148_448-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer196447,_148-448">[445]</a></sup> Highlighting Lenin's "extraordinary capacity for disciplined work" and "devotion to the revolutionary cause", Pipes noted that he exhibited much [charisma](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charisma "Charisma").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPipes1990348,_351_449-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPipes1990348,_351-449">[446]</a></sup> Similarly, Volkogonov believed that "by the very force of his personality, \[Lenin\] had an influence over people".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1994246_450-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1994246-450">[447]</a></sup> Conversely, Lenin's friend Gorky commented that in his physical appearance as a "baldheaded, stocky, sturdy person", the communist revolutionary was "too ordinary" and did not give "the impression of being a leader".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer196457_451-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer196457-451">[448]</a></sup>

Historian and biographer [Robert Service](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_Service_(historian) "Robert Service (historian)") asserted that Lenin had been an intensely emotional young man,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEService200073_452-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEService200073-452">[449]</a></sup> who exhibited strong hatred for the Tsarist authorities.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer196444Service200081_453-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer196444Service200081-453">[450]</a></sup> According to Service, Lenin developed an "emotional attachment" to his ideological heroes, such as Marx, Engels, and [Chernyshevsky](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chernyshevsky "Chernyshevsky"); he owned portraits of them,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEService2000118_454-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEService2000118-454">[451]</a></sup> and privately described himself as being "in love" with Marx and Engels.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEService2000232Lih201113_455-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEService2000232Lih201113-455">[452]</a></sup> According to Lenin biographer James D. White, Lenin treated their writings as "holy writ", a "religious dogma", which should "not be questioned but believed in".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWhite200188_456-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWhite200188-456">[453]</a></sup> In Volkogonov's view, Lenin accepted Marxism as "absolute truth", and accordingly acted like "a religious fanatic".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1994362_457-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVolkogonov1994362-457">[454]</a></sup> Similarly, Bertrand Russell felt that Lenin exhibited "unwavering faith—religious faith in the Marxian gospel".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1964409_458-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1964409-458">[455]</a></sup> Biographer Christopher Read suggested that Lenin was "a secular equivalent of theocratic leaders who derive their legitimacy from the \[perceived\] truth of their doctrines, not popular mandates".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERead2005262_459-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTERead2005262-459">[456]</a></sup> Lenin was nevertheless an [atheist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atheist "Atheist") and a [critic of religion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Criticism_of_religion "Criticism of religion"), believing that socialism was inherently atheistic; he thus considered [Christian socialism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christian_socialism "Christian socialism") a contradiction in terms.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer196440–41Volkogonov1994373Service2000149_460-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer196440%E2%80%9341Volkogonov1994373Service2000149-460">[457]</a></sup>

> \[Lenin's collected writings\] reveal in detail a man with iron will, self-enslaving self-discipline, scorn for opponents and obstacles, the cold determination of a zealot, the drive of a fanatic, and the ability to convince or browbeat weaker persons by his singleness of purpose, imposing intensity, impersonal approach, personal sacrifice, political astuteness, and complete conviction of the possession of the absolute truth. His life became the history of the Bolshevik movement.

—Biographer Louis Fischer, 1964<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer196421–22_461-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer196421%E2%80%9322-461">[458]</a></sup>

Service stated that Lenin could be "moody and volatile",<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEService2000116_462-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEService2000116-462">[459]</a></sup> and Pipes deemed him to be "a thoroughgoing misanthrope",<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPipes199611Read2005287_463-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPipes199611Read2005287-463">[460]</a></sup> a view rejected by Read, who
